Congratulations from the President of the Control Yuan on His Birthday

(Nanjing) The 31st of this month is Vice-Chairman Chiang's fiftieth birthday. The Control Yuan, through its president, respectfully composed birthday greetings to offer congratulations. The text is recorded below. "Toiling with worry for the sake of national prosperity" is an ancient teaching with validity. Our nation has already experienced the hardships of initial creation. The period of political tutelage is approaching completion, and unification is being successfully announced. The people of the nation are urged to be cautious and attend to the restoration. In the history of our nation, a new era is truly dawning, and Mr. Chiang's fiftieth birthday coincides with this moment. The people of the nation are all competing to offer aircraft as birthday gifts for Mr. Chiang. This is not just a celebration for one person or one family, but a cause for joy and encouragement for the entire nation, with voices singing praises in unison. Right-Ren has served alongside Mr. Chiang in revolutionary work, and having a relatively intimate knowledge of his life and character, it is my duty to offer words to express my heartfelt congratulations. I have often contemplated the times and admired contemporary figures. Those who link their own fate to the destiny of the era, concerned about the safety of the nation and the people, as well as the rise and fall of society, exist in every country in the world. However, Mr. Chiang, with his extraordinary talent, inherited the legacy of the Premier, leading the national revolution and shouldering the great responsibility of party affairs, military affairs, politics, and social transformation. He stands out above the common, possessing the strengths of all contemporary leaders. His divine work has been rarely matched in history. In recent years, Mr. Chiang, amidst his military and pacification efforts, has engaged in political reform and educational innovation, dedicating much effort to the cause of national revival. Therefore, I will recount a few matters for the people of the nation, so that those who admire Mr. Chiang will not only be amazed by the magnitude of his achievements but will also be convinced of the greatness of his virtue and accomplishments. When a nation stands in the world, it must have the will to rise. However, in today's turbulent international situation, the spirit and morality of the nation are essential resources for establishing a country. Our nation's politics has always emphasized civil virtue, rarely speaking of military achievements. As a result, there is a habit of valuing civil matters over military ones. Since the Tang and Song dynasties, literary composition has been used to select officials. As a result of these malpractices, scholars buried themselves in classics and became empty and impractical. They were content with inaction and gradually became weak. The vitality of the nation was thus diminished. The Qing scholar Li Shugu said, "When the spirit of writing and ink is abundant, the spirit of economics is lacking. The demise of the Song and Ming dynasties was due to this." His words are truly filled with emotion. After the opening of the seas, the utilitarian theories of Europe and Asia came along with their machinery and technology. Human desires ran rampant, and customs became extravagant. The lives of the people lost their normal course. In terms of self-cultivation, they lost their grasp of the eight virtues and four principles. In terms of behavior, they fell into a state of licentiousness and disorganization. If this continued, the nation would no longer be a nation. Mr. Chiang was deeply concerned about this, so he advocated the New Life Movement to correct the evils of the time, restoring our nation's inherent virtues from within and drawing on the civilization of the world from without. In less than two years, the wind swept through the grass. The things of muddling along and seeking temporary ease, and the behavior of seeking profit and forgetting righteousness, are already rarely seen in public society. The hearts of the people throughout the country have been revitalized. All of this is due to Mr. Chiang's accumulated diligence and dedication, disciplining himself in a regulated life, and thus being able to inspire the masses, change customs, and make great contributions to the nation and the people. Mr. Chiang also believes that the people of the nation, both in and out of government, are accustomed to being weak and indulging in a lethargic atmosphere. Their muscles and bones are becoming lax, and their physical strength is declining. Therefore, he also promoted labor service to invigorate the nation's sluggish spirit. Taking "action as the starting point" and adding the basic concepts of his revolutionary philosophy is also for this reason. Mr. Chiang believes that "action" is the only driving force for creating everything in the universe. Being proactive is the source of all prosperity for the nation, people, and society, and being passive is a good remedy for saving human corruption, laziness, and the nation's decline and danger. This is the same as the "work and training" and "labor obligations" advocated by various modern countries. The principles set by Mr. Chiang are all based on the spirit of the Chinese Kingly Way, with "altruism" and "upward progress" as their norms. Their meaning is truly vast. Mr. Chiang once said that people in the 20th century should all be independent individuals and, at the same time, social beings. Only as independent individuals can they progress upward to create their future continued life. Only as social beings should they also be altruistic to improve the well-being of all mankind. Only then can the true meaning and value of life be expressed. Therefore, the people's diligent service should not only serve the nation and society with the spirit of labor, but also the individual's life should be integrated with the life of mankind to create an eternally continuous life for mankind. These words are excellent, how broad and sincere they are! In recent years, our nation's national economy has been repeatedly attacked by the world's financial storms and has fallen into a state of acute panic. The countryside is desolate, industries are declining, financial capital is experiencing frequent crises, foreign trade is shrinking, and the lives of ordinary people are barely surviving on the road to starvation. Mr. Chiang deeply believes that this is the greatest crisis facing China today. He is deeply concerned and thinks hard to find a way for the nation to regenerate itself. Therefore, he has widely advocated the National Economic Construction Movement to awaken the nation's self-awareness, to concentrate all the forces of the government, the people, and various public and private groups, to simultaneously construct material and spiritual aspects, to alleviate the current crisis and the people's hardships. The National Economic Construction Movement is spreading throughout the country, and practical achievements are now being promoted. On the negative side, we are abolishing excessive taxes, reducing export duties, strictly prohibiting the excessive issuance of paper money, and stopping speculative activities to eliminate obstacles to the development of the national economy. On the positive side, we are improving agriculture, revitalizing agriculture, protecting minerals, adjusting labor relations, opening up roads, developing transportation construction, controlling the economy, and supporting industry and commerce, internally seeking to increase total production and solve the needs of people's livelihoods, and externally increasing export products to seek trade balance. Recently, the National Government increased the capital of the three central national banks to seek stability in the social economy and relief for agriculture, industry, and commerce. This is also the beginning of national economic construction. From this perspective, Mr. Chiang's National Economic Construction Movement plan is broad, profound, and closely aligned with the current needs of the Chinese people, and is a necessary resource for the construction of the Principle of People's Livelihood. Compared with the restoration policies currently being pursued in the United States and the five-year construction plan of Soviet Russia, it is not inferior. The domestic and international environment we are in today is more dangerous and urgent than ever before in history. External troubles are rampant, the territory is shrinking daily, and the nation is sinking and facing destruction. However, Mr. Chiang is loyal and upright, enduring humiliation and bearing heavy burdens, facing the people in a situation of blood and tears. His determination is unwavering, and he does not hesitate to take risks and overcome difficulties. He has been able to wash away flaws, dissolve divisions, and promote love and sincerity in the world. He has been able to guide the current situation of peace and unification, and the difficulties of the future may be even greater than today. I firmly believe that Mr. Chiang will be able to use his perseverance and sincerity to overcome all difficulties, control all affairs, and revive our nation and people, to complete the great cause of the Three People's Principles revolution, and to lead the four hundred million compatriots to the realm of benevolence and longevity. Therefore, I recite the poem "Nanshan You Tai" (Southern Mountain Has Arborvitae): "Happy is the prince, the light of the country. Happy is the prince, may you live ten thousand years without end." This is to celebrate the nation and also what we offer in our congratulations. (Central News Agency telegram, 30th)

The Japanese Military Exercises in Beiping and Tianjin, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Has Lodged a Protest

Forcibly Occupying Civilian Houses and Cutting Off Transportation, Illegal, Unreasonable, and Shocking

(Nanjing) Since the 26th of this month, the "military" stationed in Beiping, Tianjin, and other places has been conducting large-scale exercises for ten days, centered on Fengtai, including Beiping, Tianjin, and the northern section of the Pinghan Railway. The number of participating troops has reached more than 7,000. They have forcibly occupied hundreds of civilian houses in the suburbs of Tianjin, forcing out residents. At the same time, they have conscripted civilian laborers, firewood, and other items, causing great disturbance. The continuous tense exercises have cut off transportation in the nearby areas. Most of the civilian houses in the Dazhigu and Shicheng areas have been damaged, and crops have also been cut down. It is truly shocking that foreign troops in our country's territory have taken such illegal and unreasonable actions. It is reported that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs believes that the Japanese military's actions violate treaties and international law and undermine our country's sovereignty, and has sent a note to the Japanese Embassy to protest. (Central News Agency telegram, 30th)

The Truth About the Japanese Forcibly Renting Civilian Houses and Causing Trouble in Taiyuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Has Lodged a Protest with the Japanese Side, the Tianjin Japanese Consulate Has Sent Police to Taiyuan Urgently, Japanese Police Are Still Stationed at Tanaka's House

(Nanjing) The city house at No. 4 Ansi Street in Taiyuan was previously verbally rented by Wang Junde, a Hebei native, from the landlord. However, the landlord discovered that Wang had a background and often ordered him to find a reliable guarantor to ensure that he would not rent the house on behalf of others. Wang avoided showing his face because he had no reliable guarantor. Suddenly, two Japanese, Takeada Sueo and Tanaka Yoshitaro, forcibly occupied the house, claiming that they had entrusted Wang to rent the house and intended to set up a business. The two sides were unable to reach a decision. Then, Takeada left Taiyuan for Tianjin, and Tanaka frequently came to the house to inspect it. On the 26th of this month, Takeada returned to Jin and occupied the house again. On the 27th, the Jin authorities, together with the street chief, the deputy street chief, and the Japanese servant, counted and sealed the medicines and equipment in the house that were inconvenient to carry and temporarily stored them in the room. They escorted Takeada Sueo to the Japanese Consulate in Zhengzhou, and the landlord and the police bricked up the door and sent police to patrol it. Then, Tanaka Yoshitaro suddenly gathered five Japanese, including Otsugake Takezo, Yamada Yoshiichi, etc., wearing military uniforms and carrying pistols, broke open the bricked door, occupied the house, drank alcohol, made noise, and threw bricks at the street, breaking the glass of nearby shops. They also hung a wooden sign at the door, written in Japanese, meaning that the house was temporarily managed by the Japanese army for reasons. This is the truth about the Japanese forcibly renting houses and causing trouble in Taiyuan. It is reported that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has lodged a protest with the Japanese side. The Japanese Allied News Agency's claim that there is anti-Japanese sentiment in Taiyuan and that Shanxi officials are expelling Japanese merchants is obviously inconsistent with the facts. (Central News Agency telegram, 30th)

(Tianjin) The investigator Cheng Maoyu, from the Taiyuan Japanese Police Outpost, came to Tianjin on the 30th to report that the Hezhong Company, established by Tanaka, was located at No. 1 Fangyou East Lane in Taiyuan. Next door was the Xieshan Hospital, established by Wang Junde, a Chinese. At the end of July, the Xieshan Hospital moved to Anshijie, and Wang privately rented the former site to Tanaka to convert it into a drug dealership. The Taiyuan ban prohibited private rentals to Japanese, so someone reported it, and the court ruled that the house should be returned to the original owner for rent. Tanaka refused, and a dispute arose this month when the court enforced the order. (Special telegram, 30th)

(Tianjin) Nishi, a secretary at the Japanese Consulate in Taiyuan, sent a telegram to the Tianjin Consulate on the 30th reporting the current situation of the Japanese residents, saying that 32 men and women were being housed at the Takahashi Mansion and requesting more police protection. Japanese police are stationed at both Tanaka Yoshitaro's Hezhong Company and residence. According to the Tianjin Japanese Consulate, there are a total of 29 Japanese residents and 4 Koreans in Taiyuan, and they are all safe. (Special telegram, 30th)

(Tianjin) Guan Chuan, an official from the Tianjin Japanese Consulate who was dispatched to investigate the Hezhong Foreign Company case, went to Beiping on the morning of the 30th and rushed to Taiyuan with six policemen from the Beiping Police Department. (Special telegram, 30th)

(Beiping) The autumn exercise of the Japanese garrison in North China was on its fifth day, the 30th. The 1st Regiment of the Japanese army stationed in Beiping and Fengtai and the 2nd Regiment of the Japanese army stationed in Tongzhou and Tianjin held a resistance exercise on the 30th. The 1st Regiment, consisting of more than 400 infantry and artillery soldiers from the Japanese army stationed in Beiping, left the Japanese barracks through Yongdingmen at 5:30 a.m. on the 30th, along with seven tanks, twenty trucks loaded with military supplies, and four motorcycle sidecars, and headed on foot to Anding via the southern suburbs. A unit of about 400 Japanese infantry soldiers and more than 30 cavalry soldiers also left Tai'anmen at 5:30 a.m., along with more than ten carts loaded with food, and headed on foot to Anding via the southern suburbs, where they gathered with more than 800 Japanese soldiers stationed in the area of ​​Sihezhuang and Zhangzhuangchang. At the same time, the 2nd Regiment, consisting of the Japanese army stationed in Tianjin and the Japanese army stationed in Tongzhou, also departed from Langfang and Tongxian around 6 a.m. on the 30th and arrived at Longjiachang and Hejiafen in the Tongxian boundary to gather. Starting at 9 a.m., the two regiments moved together to conduct a confrontation exercise. At about 10 a.m., the two regiments encountered each other in the Dahuan Village and Majuqiao area and engaged in an encounter battle, holding out until 5 p.m., when the Tianjin-Tongzhou Japanese army retreated eastward, and the Beiping-Fengtai Japanese army followed forward until the exercise ended at 5 p.m. They camped and had dinner in Mazhuang and Saoziying. Starting at 9 p.m., they continued the night battle. More than 30 liaison officers, including Zhao Botao and Liu Qiufu, dispatched by political and other agencies, arrived by car from Fengtai to the area of ​​Dahongmen and Xiaohongmen in the southern suburbs at about 5 a.m. yesterday to take care of the Japanese army in the exercise area. The 1st and 2nd Regiments of the Japanese army are scheduled to continue the confrontation exercise in the northeast area of ​​Saoziying starting tomorrow morning, camping in Xiaogaozhuang and Sujiafen that night, and conducting the confrontation exercise in the original location for one day. The regimental confrontation will end that evening, (30th Dispatch)

Xingzhong Company Plans to Plant Cotton and Purchase Land in the Puppet Hebei-East Zone

(Tianjin) Xingdong Company plans to purchase 500,000 mu of land in the puppet Hebei-East Zone to establish the North China Cotton Association, plant cotton, and establish a cotton experiment farm in Tongzhou to improve cultivation, gather 430,000 farmers, and aim to produce 500,000 bales of high-quality cotton annually, (30th Dispatch)

Special Issue for Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's Fiftieth Birthday

Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's Family Education and Academic Cultivation

— Shao Yuanchong

Written for Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's Fiftieth Birthday

Historians, when observing central figures of an era, should not only understand the greatness of their achievements but also recognize their usual thoughts and academic cultivation. They should not only pay close attention to the characteristics of their personality but also deeply understand the family environment and family education that shaped these characteristics. Based on the above two conditions, I would like to provide a faithful description of Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's family education and academic cultivation, as far as I know, to the comrades and compatriots who respect him.

Twenty-five years before the founding of the Republic of China (Dinghai year in the lunar calendar - 1887 in the solar calendar), Mr. Chiang Kai-shek was born in Xikou Town, Jinxi, Fenghua, Zhejiang. That year, Sun Yat-sen transferred from Guangzhou to the Hong Kong College of Medicine for Chinese, affiliated with the Alice Ho Miu Ling Nethersole Hospital, and discussed revolution with classmates such as Chen Shaobai and Lu Haodong.

Most of Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's ancestors were farmers. His grandfather, Duke Yu Biao, changed to engaging in commerce, especially managing the salt and tea industries, and the family's livelihood gradually became prosperous. Duke Yu Biao was also a kind-hearted elder who helped relatives and friends with weddings, funerals, or emergencies. He also fully supported local public welfare undertakings, such as road repairs and dike construction, and personally supervised them to ensure their perfection. The area near Jinxi where he lived was the junction of Ningbo, Shaoxing, and Taizhou prefectures. There was a ridge called Wuling, which was a necessary passage for people from the three prefectures. Because the area was desolate and sparsely populated, there were no teahouses or places to eat. Duke Yu Biao prepared dry food and tea at the Buddhist temple on the ridge to provide for passersby, without interruption for many years, and the passersby were very grateful. Duke Yu Biao was also knowledgeable in medicine and often treated people. He also liked to study Buddhism, thus promoting his spirit of benevolence and universal love to help people and save the world. He was strict in managing the family but kind to people. Mr. Chiang Kai-shek was often sick in his childhood, and Duke Yu Biao often treated him himself and cherished him very much. Therefore, Mr. Chiang Kai-shek had a deep impression of Duke Yu Biao in his childhood, and Duke Yu Biao's virtues of strict family management, kindness to people, and dedication to society had a great influence on Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's later cultivation.

Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's father, Duke Su'an, was straightforward in nature, fair in dealing with affairs, sincere in treating people, self-disciplined and thrifty, and had a resolute appearance. Compared with Duke Yu Biao, he was more masculine in character. When Duke Yu Biao was managing the salt industry, the family was quite wealthy. However, when Duke Su'an was in his teens, it was during the reigns of Emperor Daoguang and Emperor Xianfeng of the Qing Dynasty. The Taiping Rebellion rose, and Zhejiang was often a battleground for the Taiping Army and the Qing Army. As a result, the local area was devastated, and all industries were abandoned. Duke Yu Biao's lifelong management of the salt industry was also destroyed. Later, when the military situation in Zhejiang stabilized slightly, Duke Su'an inherited his father's ambition to revitalize the salt industry, giving full play to his capable abilities. In just a few years, he completely restored it. In his hometown, he liked to mediate disputes and uphold justice, and he worked hard for public welfare undertakings. He also made every effort to promote local education and provided assistance to many people who sought education without funds, thus cultivating a large number of talents. Regarding family education, he once said to Mr. Chiang Kai-shek and his brothers: "Because I inherited the legacy of my ancestors in my youth, I cannot serve the country to the best of my ability. However, I still wish to make considerable efforts in local public welfare, education, and improving customs, so that the local area can be peaceful and the family can be harmonious. You can concentrate on studying, and if you achieve something in the future, you can also make up for my shortcomings." This sincere family instruction greatly moved Mr. Chiang Kai-shek and his brothers. Although Duke Su'an loved his sons very much in his later years, he still taught and supervised them very strictly and had even higher expectations. Therefore, Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's later efforts in his studies and national affairs were indeed closely related to Duke Su'an's family education. Duke Su'an had so many virtues and characteristics that greatly influenced Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's spirit. Unfortunately, due to lifelong hard work, he was unable to enjoy a long life and passed away at the age of fifty-three. At that time, Mr. Chiang Kai-shek was only nine years old, and his grief can be imagined.

Mr. Chiang Kai-shek not only deeply benefited from the family education of his grandfather and father in his youth but also greatly influenced by the teachings of his mother, Madam Wang. Because Mr. Chiang Kai-shek lost his father at a young age, Madam Wang took on the responsibilities of both parents, teaching her son tirelessly. When he made mistakes, she would severely reprimand and punish him without any leniency. When Mr. Chiang Kai-shek went out to study at the age of thirteen, Madam Wang tearfully instructed him: "Since your father's death, I have worked hard to educate you, not because I want you to seize high office and possess great wealth, but because I hope you will love yourself for the country and preserve the good name of your ancestors." She often gave such instructions, so Mr. Chiang Kai-shek was very moved. When Mr. Chiang Kai-shek went to Japan to study military science at the age of eighteen, Madam Wang greatly praised him and raised travel expenses and tuition fees to enable him to make the trip. She also made the family life more frugal so that tuition fees would not be lacking. In the autumn of the Xinhai Revolution, the Wuchang Revolutionary Army rose up, and the Jiangzhe area also continued to respond. At that time, Mr. Chiang Kai-shek was supervising the army in the Shanghai-Hangzhou area. When relatives and friends in his hometown heard the news, they were mostly extremely frightened, but Madam Wang was not panicked at all and said, "A man serves the country, and death is death. What is there to worry about?" Later, when Jiangzhe was restored and news of victory reached home, Madam Wang remained calm and continued to warn him in her family letters to do his best for the country and never slacken. When Mr. Chiang Kai-shek was in Shanghai, although he repeatedly decided to welcome her to live with him, Madam Wang only stayed for a few days and returned to her hometown to live her simple life. When the revolution failed for the second time, Mr. Chiang Kai-shek fled overseas. He once wrote to his mother in a public and urgent manner, and Madam Wang tried her best to help him. She did not listen to those who advised him to return north, and everyone admired her courageous and compassionate spirit. Sun Yat-sen presented a horizontal plaque inscribed "Educating Children with Excellence" in the fifth year of the Republic of China to praise her. She continued to carry on Duke Su'an's ambition to devote herself to local public welfare and education and to help her relatives and clansmen. She also liked to study Buddhist scriptures, and she was able to understand the essentials of the Surangama Sutra, the Vimalakirti Sutra, and the Diamond Sutra, which also had a significant impact on her self-cultivation.

Since Mr. Chiang Kai-shek received strict family education from his grandparents and parents from his youth to adulthood, he already had a solid foundation for physical and mental self-cultivation. The inherited qualities of eagerness for public good and righteousness were also the innate seeds for his later efforts in national affairs. All of his characteristics, such as his strong personality, passionate emotions, courageous spirit, and simple life, were related to his family instructions. From this, it can be seen how close the relationship between family education and personality cultivation is.

According to what Mr. Chiang Kai-shek told me before, his revolutionary sentiments were cultivated because, after his ancestors moved to Zhejiang after the fall of the Ming Dynasty, the Qing Dynasty ruled China, and Chiang's ancestors had left instructions warning their descendants not to become Qing officials. Therefore, this became an important precept in family education. Later, after Mr. Chiang Kai-shek went to Japan to study, he was guided by Sun Yat-sen and joined the Tongmenghui. He had a deeper understanding of the great cause of revolution. Later, he became friends with Mr. Chen Qimei and others, so his revolutionary sentiments became even more passionate. However, the initial seeds of his revolutionary thought can also be said to be closely related to family education.

The above narration provides a deep understanding of the relationship between Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's temperament, the cultivation of revolutionary thought, and his family education. Now, let's briefly describe Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's academic cultivation.

Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's attitude towards learning is to work hard and do practical things. He never hopes to use simple, labor-saving, and time-saving methods to obtain a deep academic foundation. He applied the learning methods of many scholars in the past, such as circling and marking a book from beginning to end, writing notes, adding marginal notes, and using red pens to highlight or mark the key points in the book. He used these methods to carefully study many books that he considered essential to read carefully. His greatest regret in the setbacks of the Dongjiang military campaign in the eleventh and twelfth years of the Republic of China was the loss of several diaries and several books that had been annotated and circled. In the study at his home in Fenghua, the principal's office of the Huangpu Military Academy in Guangzhou, and some of his personal books, many kinds of books can be found that have been circled, annotated, and marked with attention symbols in red and blue pens. These are all the results of his hard work in learning.

In his early years, in order to develop a habit of perseverance, Mr. Chiang Kai-shek wrote a diary every day. It can be said that there has been no interruption in the past twenty years. Although he cannot write in great detail due to busy schedules, he always writes a few lines or a few sentences every day. In addition to recording events and the books he has read, the content of his diary also faithfully records his self-examination of his temperament and self-cultivation, such as whether his temperament is impetuous, whether he is overly harsh to others and makes them feel embarrassed, whether distracting thoughts arise from time to time, and so on. As for the records of the secret period in Shanghai, he often used hidden language to represent them. For example, when the Zhaohe warship launched an attack in Shanghai in the winter of the fourth year of the Republic of China, the diary used "school meeting" to represent "Zhaohe launched" and "ringing the bell in the auditorium" to represent "the navy opened fire." Therefore, if this extremely historically valuable handwritten diary is published in the future, many facts and hidden languages ​​in it may have to be explained by Mr. Chiang Kai-shek himself.

In addition to Sun Yat-sen's complete legacy, Mr. Chiang Kai-shek has benefited the most from the writings of Wang Yangming and Zeng Guofan in terms of basic books on self-cultivation. Mr. Chiang Kai-shek not only systematically read and annotated the complete works of these two families from beginning to end but also repeatedly read and reviewed them and could be said to be never tired of reading them. Yangming and Xiangxiang both created achievements in difficult times, which gave Mr. Chiang Kai-shek a great spiritual encouragement when he encountered difficulties and setbacks. Sun Yat-sen's lifelong struggle, especially the dozens of days of hardship in Guangzhou, provided a genuine training in practice, which was the most beneficial part of his life. Of course, Mr. Chiang Kai-shek has read many books in the past decades, but the basic books that he has read carefully are only about thirty kinds. Now, I will list the catalogue of books that he himself listed and selected for reading in the past few years:

Five Classics, Four Books, Confucius' Family Sayings, Zuo Zhuan, Strategies of the Warring States, Six Secret Teachings, Sun Tzu, Wu Tzu, Zhuangzi, Han Feizi, Chu Ci, Records of the Grand Historian, Zizhi Tongjian, History of the Qing Dynasty, Western History, History of the European War, History of the Franco-Prussian War, History of Napoleon's Wars, History of the Russo-Japanese War, Barker's Tactics, Various Military Science Studies, Just War Theory, Asian Geography, World Geography, Ancient Prose Compilation, Various Collections of Zhuge Liang, Yue Wu Mu, Wen Tianxiang, and Qi Jiguang, Complete Works of Zeng Guofan, Complete Works of Hu Linyi, Collection of Zuo Zongtang, Collection of Luo Bingzhang, Collection of Li Hongzhang, History of Chinese Philosophy, Psychology, Statistics, Sociology, Economics

Analyzing the contents of the above-listed thirty-odd kinds of books, it can be said that they include Chinese ethical thought, Chinese political philosophy, Chinese history and world history, Chinese military science principles and world military science, Chinese literature, Chinese and foreign geography, and a portion of basic social sciences. If they can be integrated and understood, they can indeed create the basic theories of politics. These dozens of books are the foundation of Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's academic cultivation, and I hope everyone will carefully understand them.

The above narration is just a fragment of Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's academic cultivation and family education, but it can prove that those who want to emulate Mr. Chiang Kai-shek should work hard in his actual life, in his actual efforts, from the plain, arduous, and subtle aspects. In general, fathers and brothers who want to cultivate their children into talents should also emulate Mr. Chiang Kai-shek's respectful family education, loving but not condoning, and give their children an example of how to be a person in everything they do. In this way, even if the children do not necessarily have extraordinary achievements in the future, at least they can become people who are disciplined and self-reliant and will not burden society. The survival, development, and progress of a country certainly require a few leaders who can overcome difficulties to shoulder heavy responsibilities, but they also require a large number of good citizens who are eager for public good, abide by the law, are generous and helpful, and are self-reliant and self-sufficient to maintain social stability. This is an additional hope at the end of this article, and I hope readers will pay attention to it.

Our Newspaper's Dedication

In the year of Rou Zhao Kundun, in the month of Wu She according to the lunar calendar, it is the fiftieth birthday of Mr. Chiang Kai-shek of Fenghua, the current President of the Executive Yuan and Chairman of the Military Commission. Officials and guests, together, devise a dedication. Banging on the earth and holding pens, we sing of the grace and achievements of the Duke, continuing the harmony and composing odes to his longevity. Both paper drunk with gold and smoke and mist congeal. Heaven bestows pure blessings, giving you great prosperity. Parallel to the grand ceremony, nothing can surpass this. It is only because you were born with extraordinary talent, in a time of turmoil. As a top candidate for a national defense barrier, you have long held the reins of the country. Bright wings soothing and pacifying, diligently noted. Your reputation reaches distant lands, and your achievements are preserved in the annals. Rejoicing in the year of accurate virtue, we increase our thoughts of what is far away. Although the wind and rain are like darkness, the cock crows incessantly. Praising merit and recounting virtue, expressing reverence. Caring about customs and cherishing hearts, expressing our wishes. May gold and stone be forever solid, and fragrance and splendor increase. With pens adorned, we present our words, acting as our voice. We respectfully offer this ode:

Oh, our Duke, majestic Wuling, with brilliant talent from a young age, also with a virtuous mother, encountering turbulent times, leading a strong army, traveling to the north and south, pacifying the borderlands, relying on your prestige. The people's livelihood is fragile, like your solid talent, singing without forgetting encouragement. A great vessel of the nation, flowing Jinxi, practicing family teachings, diligent and earnest in mind, rising up and wielding authority, all who are approached submit, our martial power is displayed, nothing is too far to reach, implementing policies, with verbal instructions, indeed endowed by heaven, with benevolent intentions, skillfully managing worldly affairs, possessing spiritual brilliance and virtue, diligent in work, face-to-face instructions, like an awl in a bag, all the chiefs are arrogant, to the utmost of our strength, admired by all, both high and low are content, the masses are bewildered, suffering and illness are embraced, you must discern this, do not waver in your will, with this good foundation, continue to strive tirelessly, strive to be a complete person, become a hero among men, gladly obeying the department, followed by air travel, all who hear your voice, will not fail to obey, waiting for you to revive, you should enjoy longevity, for thousands of autumns and ten thousand springs.

Striving for National Survival by Concentrating National Strength and Supporting the Leader

— Wu Tiecheng

—Speech at the Shanghai National Military Training Association's Dinner Celebrating Chairman Chiang's Fiftieth Birthday—

Today, all comrades in Shanghai who are responsible for national military education and civic training are holding a dinner party here to celebrate Chairman Chiang's fiftieth birthday. We should have a deep understanding of the significance of this grand celebration.

Comrades, what is China most in need of today? What China most needs today is:

An enlightened leader;

A party with principles;

A strong and powerful government.

If we have an enlightened leader, a party with principles, and a strong and powerful government, not only can the current serious national crisis be resolved, but even if it is ten times more serious, we can have the strength to overcome it!

In the past, our general public did not clearly understand the conditions for saving the country from its difficulties. Therefore, we could not concentrate all our strength to contribute to the leader, and our leader had no way to use the strength of the whole country to overcome the current environment and resolve the current national crisis. If, ten years ago, our people had such awareness, knowing to support the leader, support the party, and support the government, I dare to believe that today's national crisis would never have occurred; even if it had, it would have been overcome and resolved long ago!

However, the people now are awakened: they have deeply recognized the seriousness of the national crisis; they have deeply recognized the way to save the country from its difficulties; they are ready to sacrifice everything, and willingly and sincerely contribute all their strength to our leader, to be used by our leader: so that our leader can use this majestic and great strength to save the current crisis and revive our nation. This is not an overly optimistic fantasy, but a reality in practice. Just look at the recent awareness of Chairman Chiang's fiftieth birthday among our people across the country, and you can see the proof. The people, who never cared about national affairs, are now extremely excited; whether men, women, old, or young, almost everyone knows about Chairman Chiang's fiftieth birthday; they all know to express their respect for Chairman Chiang; they all believe that Chairman Chiang is a persevering and outstanding leader, and the savior of the nation and the country. This kind of national unity and enthusiastic support of the people was expressed even more thoroughly at the naming ceremony of the Zhongzheng Squadron held in this city a few days ago. That day, we had over ten thousand people at the Longhua Airport. Why did over ten thousand people come to participate in the naming ceremony that day? Were they just there to watch the excitement? No, they were there to participate in the naming ceremony of the Zhongzheng Squadron aircraft, because the significance of the Zhongzheng Squadron naming ceremony is very significant; it is a solemn ceremony to strengthen national power and consolidate national defense. From the manifestation of the national spirit that day, we can say that the Chinese people now have recognition, have awareness, know how to support the leader, support the party, and support the government; they have recognized that these three conditions must be met; with these three conditions, the country can be revived. And among these three conditions, the most important is still people. As the ancient saying goes: "He who gains the people will prosper." Therefore, we must have an enlightened leader in order to establish a strong party and government. Although the national crisis is very serious now, we are very optimistic; we already have a persevering and outstanding, enlightened leader who leads the people; our 450 million people across the country can also unanimously express their enthusiasm for support; willingly and sincerely willing to concentrate all their strength and contribute it to the leader, so that our leader can use this powerful force to deal with and overcome the current national crisis!

Everyone here is responsible for military education, and military education is the most important part of public education. The fact that the people of Shanghai have such awareness today, and have such recognition of the leader, the party, and the government, cannot but be attributed to the efforts of your work. Therefore, I should express my respect for your past achievements today. However, the work ahead is even more arduous. Today, we must seek survival from death. Only when 450 million compatriots can concentrate their strength, support the leader, and sacrifice for the country, will the country have a way to survive, and the nation can be revived. Therefore, we cannot but hope that you will redouble your efforts in the future! Finally, let us shout loudly:

Long live Chairman Chiang!

Long live the Chinese Kuomintang!

Long live the Republic of China!

Chiang Kai-shek's Fiftieth Birthday

— Yu Feipeng

October 31st, the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China, is the fiftieth birthday of Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Commission and concurrently President of the Executive Yuan. The International Propaganda Department of the Central Party Headquarters plans to publish a special collection of congratulatory articles. I, Peng, was asked to contribute an article. I humbly believe that Chairman Chiang's achievements in recreating the Republic of China and unifying China are almost universally known, seen, and spoken of by the people of the country. There is no need for me, Peng, to describe even a fraction of them.

However, my relationship with Chairman Chiang is that we were from the same village in our youth and have been under his command for a long time. I have followed him on the battlefield for nearly twenty years. Having been close to him for a long time, I deeply know that what distinguishes him from ordinary people is not only his outstanding talent and strategy, but also his great personality. The reason why he can cultivate this great personality is entirely due to the two virtues of loyalty and filial piety.

Chairman Chiang is naturally intelligent, with unparalleled perseverance. He was rich in national revolutionary ideas in his early years. After joining the Tongmenghui in the late Qing Dynasty, he first followed Chen Qimei in launching an uprising in Shanghai, achieving remarkable military successes. Then, he followed President Sun Yat-sen, on the one hand, dedicating himself to military construction, establishing a revolutionary foundation, and on the other hand, planning military expeditions to eliminate warlords in the North and South, exhausting his wisdom and considering success or failure, gain or loss, life or death as secondary, in order to assist President Sun, support the Three Principles of the People, and consolidate the party and the country. Chairman Chiang's loyalty is no less than that of ancient national heroes and sages.

Chairman Chiang lost his father in his childhood, and Madame Wang worked hard to raise and educate him. She allowed him to study in foreign countries and permitted him to devote himself to the revolution. Chairman Chiang was exceptionally filial and able to anticipate and carry out her wishes in serving Madame Wang. He never violated her instructions, and never acted presumptuously in matters she forbade. Within the family, there was harmony and joyfulness for decades, as the villagers knew and admired. As an ancient sage said, "To seek loyal subjects, one must look to the families of filial sons." Therefore, Chairman Chiang's ability to be loyal to the country and fulfill his responsibility to save the country is also an extension of his filial piety.

The depravity of people's hearts and the corruption of customs have reached their peak today. Based on his inherent nature and long-standing practices, Chairman Chiang intends to use the principles of loyalty and filial piety to save people's hearts and customs, and to cultivate the nation's vitality. This is truly prescribing the right medicine for the disease, something that ordinary politicians cannot aspire to. What we sincerely pray for is that Chairman Chiang's great strategy for saving the country will be widely implemented throughout the world and achieve complete success. By saving the country to prolong the country's life, Chairman Chiang's great personality will also last as long as the country. This is what I, Peng, want to say. Yu Feipeng, Acting Minister of the Ministry of Transportation and Communications

A Collection of Chairman Chiang's Recent Two Years of Words and Deeds

— Tao Guoren

This month, on the 31st, we respectfully celebrate Chairman Chiang's fiftieth birthday. People from all walks of life joyfully offer their congratulations. However, Chairman Chiang insisted on humility and was unwilling to burden the people with expenses for his personal birthday. Therefore, he issued instructions that, in addition to congratulatory messages, no gifts should be accepted (all birthday plaques, scrolls, etc. received by the Military Commission in recent days have been returned to the senders). However, the act of purchasing aircraft to celebrate his birthday expresses the sincerity of supporting the leader and increases the country's ability to resist aggression, truly an unprecedented event. Recalling that Chairman Chiang worries about national affairs and has no time to rest, especially in recent years, feeling the devastation of the Communist bandits internally and the encroachment of friendly nations externally, he often goes to various places to personally give instructions. Therefore, his usual wise words and exemplary actions are abundant. Thus, I respectfully compile this brief collection to provide the people of the country, in this time of national crisis, with a deep recollection of the leader's virtue and hard work.

The Twenty-fourth Year of the Republic of China

New Year's Day, attended the oath-taking ceremony of the committee members of the Zhejiang Provincial Government and gave a speech, "Whether it is the problems of individuals or the country, they should be eliminated as much as possible." After the ceremony, he returned to Fenghua.

January 15th, left Ningbo and flew to Shanghai, visited the city area, and paid respects at the tomb of Madame Song.

January 18th, returned to Nanjing to meet with officials and received the head of Ningxia Education, instructing him to implement universal education.

January 25th, sent a telegram to the Xinjiang authorities, hoping that they would report the employment of Russian advisors and the loan contract in detail to the Central Government to dispel rumors.

Chairman Chiang, believing that women's loose hair and permed hair in various cities were harmful to health, specially issued a handwritten order to prohibit it.

February 1st, received Japanese Minister Arida and Lieutenant General Suzuki, and talked to reporters about Sino-Japanese relations.

February 1st, the Nanchang Headquarters was dissolved at the end of last month due to the pacification of Ruijin and the end of the military operations against the bandits in Jiangxi Province.

Current Affairs Commentary

How to Deal with the Current Food Problem

— Liu

Since the new crops of soybeans, wheat, rice, and grains came onto the market this year, prices have been rising continuously, attracting attention from all quarters. Some argue that the reason for the price increase is due to banks investing in rural areas, undertaking grain mortgage loans, and the development of agricultural warehouses in various provinces, leading to large stockpiles. Furthermore, many farmers, having had a good harvest, are hoarding surplus grain to sell at a higher price, or are worried about drought and disaster, and are scrambling to store up reserves, resulting in soaring grain prices. If this is indeed the case, it is a welcome phenomenon. For if there is truly a bumper harvest, accumulating surplus grain to guard against famine years is an excellent practice. Moreover, if prices rise due to stockpiling, and rise to the point of harming the people's current food supply, the stockpiling will inevitably stop, or they will even release their stored grain to stabilize prices. This not only does not hinder the people's food supply, but also has the benefit of regulation. Therefore, the temporary rise in grain prices is not a cause for great concern. However, if the purpose of stockpiling is for other reasons, such as hoarding for profit or using it for manipulation, with extravagant hopes of profiting, then the higher the grain price, the firmer their determination to hoard. Even if the market reports a grain shortage and people are struggling to find food, it would be impossible to move the minds of such people. If the reason for the soaring prices lies here, then it is truly a cause for concern and requires alternative effective measures. As for farmers thinking of selling at a higher price due to a surplus from a good harvest, or thinking of stockpiling grain to prevent hunger due to the increasing autumn drought, given the current economic capacity of the average farmer, they would be an absolute minority. Even if they do hoard, the quantity would be very small and unlikely to be the main cause of rising grain prices.

During the meeting of the eight provinces and cities on food issues, the Shanghai representative proposed establishing a grain transportation and sales bureau to regulate the people's food supply and stabilize grain prices. Preparations were eventually moved to the Ministry of Finance due to the large sums of money and the magnitude of the undertaking. Recently, the government also discussed issues such as establishing a food authority and banning food exports, with talks of immediately convening meetings of relevant ministries and commissions. The provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang also believe that the recent rise in grain prices is partly due to grain merchants smuggling grain, and have taken measures to strictly prohibit food exports. The Shanghai grain industry believes that this matter obstructs circulation and hinders the people's food supply in Shanghai, and is calling for the ban to be lifted. All of these are direct consequences of the rising grain prices.

There are many ways to address the issue of the people's food supply; how could this short commentary cover them all? In short, the rise in grain prices today is like "when Copper Mountain collapses in the east, the Luoyang bell rings in the west." Grain prices in production and sales areas rise in response to each other, so it is not a matter of one place rising while another place falls, requiring transportation and sales for adjustment. Therefore, while transportation and sales are an important aspect of resolving the people's food supply, they are not the most urgent task at present. If, on the one hand, we are talking about transportation and sales, emphasizing circulation, and on the other hand, we are restricting exports, what is the meaning of this? It is important to understand that the crux of the problem today does not seem to lie in banning exports. In recent years, rice and grain have been continuously transported to the north, which we have long considered a cause for concern. As the saying goes, "The benefit of using troops lies in taking from the people and feeding on the enemy," so that there is no worry of "distant transport impoverishing the army" (see this newspaper's current commentary on March 11). Therefore, even if a ban is implemented, can we be certain that the other party will not resort to the old trick of smuggling? Moreover, with China's doors wide open and smuggling still prevalent, can we be even more certain that after reaching the shore, it will not be transshipped elsewhere? Even if there are no such concerns and we resolutely implement the ban, it must be a nationwide ban on exports, with prevention also on land routes, before it can be effective. Otherwise, smuggling will still be unstoppable. If we implement inspections of grain crossing borders, then we worry about harassing merchants. Restricting circulation between provinces not only opens the door to obstruction but also risks losing the benefits of regulation if others follow suit. Moreover, with adjacent lands forming interlocking patterns, and provinces separated by a single stream, the borders between them are like those between disparate regions. Although it does not amount to cutting off grain supplies, the inconvenience is already enough to hinder the circulation of food.

For the current situation, besides the transportation and sales and stockpiling of grain, which should be discussed separately, I believe we should pay attention to the following points: (1) The current Baojia system is being vigorously promoted, making it easy to complete the survey of food production in a short period of time. On the other hand, by surveying the quantity sold at the collection and distribution ports of food, we can obtain more accurate figures on food production and sales, which can be used as a basis for regulation. (2) How to reduce the control of external forces over the grain market and how to practically manage it to prevent manipulation by speculators should be planned and implemented immediately. (3) Public stockpiling should be implemented to prevent merchants from hoarding for profit while encouraging stockpiling. (4) Food management agencies should be established at food collection and distribution ports. These agencies should not be composed of various parties but must have dedicated personnel responsible for managing all food-related matters in cooperation with officials and merchants. (5) If, at present, it is believed that grain prices are already high and should be slightly restrained, then please ask the banking sector to temporarily refrain from making various promotions for investing in rural areas and stockpiling grain to reassure speculators and national households, and temporarily stop buying to ease market tension. As for the extent of the bumper harvest, whether there is a surplus or still a shortage, we must formulate a comprehensive plan. We should not be overly cautious or take things too lightly but should prioritize the public welfare and seek solutions based on facts.

UEDA Kenkichi Meets NAMI Jirō, Discusses Manchukuo-Korea Cooperation, Strengthening Security, and Developing Resources

Seoul - The Governor-General of South Korea and his party departed Unggi at 8:00 AM on the 29th, traveled along the banks of the Tumen River, and arrived in Tumen at 4:25 PM. They dined with Commander Ueda of the Kwantung Army at the consular branch office and held important discussions from 5:00 PM until 7:30 PM, resuming the discussions at 8:00 PM and concluding at 10:40 PM. (Kyodo Telegram, 30th)

Tumen - When the two generals, NAMI and Ueda, met with the press corps, Governor-General NAMI stated to the reporters regarding the content of the meeting: "Commander Ueda of the Kwantung Army and I happened to be conducting our initial inspections at the same time, separated only by the border. We considered this a good opportunity, so we held a meeting. The content of the discussions cannot be disclosed at this time. In essence, we fully discussed the inseparable economic relationship and the issue of strengthening security based on the principle of Manchukuo-Korea unity." After further discussions from 8:00 PM, the two generals issued a joint statement, stating: "Governor-General NAMI of South Korea is inspecting North Korea, and Commander Ueda of the Kwantung Army is simultaneously inspecting the JianDao area. Both sides considered this a good opportunity and thus held a meeting. Governor-General NAMI obtained the Emperor's approval and arrived in Tumen at 4:00 PM on the 29th, where he met with Commander Ueda at the consular branch office. Both sides believe that this will greatly benefit the future relationship between Korea and Manchukuo. The accompanying generals also held thorough discussions on matters under their respective jurisdictions." (Kyodo Telegram, 30th)

British Government Resolves to Strictly Curtail Fascist Activities

(London) - Home Secretary Lloyd declared in the House of Commons today that the British government will make every effort to prohibit Fascism and anti-Semitism. The "mischievous actions" of the London Fascists must be prohibited. (National Telegram, 29th)

Government Forces Launch Counteroffensive, Madrid's Situation Stabilizes, Using Tanks and Aircraft in Combat, Three Towns South of the Capital Recovered

Madrid - According to government announcements, government forces have achieved significant victories after launching a major counteroffensive in the southern and southeastern sectors of the Madrid front. Government forces have recaptured the three towns of Torrejón de Velasco, La Guardia, and Ciempozuelos. The Nationalist Revolutionary Army had been preparing to launch a final offensive on the capital from these three towns. In addition, government forces have completely controlled the railway line between Madrid and Aranjuez and are currently advancing towards Illescas, located 25 miles from the capital. A military bulletin detailing the campaign stated that government forces had made great progress on the southern front as a result of the counteroffensive, forcing the Nationalist Revolutionary Army to transfer infantry, artillery units, and Moroccan cavalry reinforcements from other fronts. In the past three days, government aircraft have shot down thirty Nationalist Revolutionary Army aircraft on the northern, northwestern, and southwestern fronts. Although Madrid has not announced definitive news, the atmosphere in the city seems to be gradually calming down. Prime Minister Caballero has issued a startling official statement, stating that the militia is now prepared to advance safely because they have tanks and ample munitions, and that they will remove the danger from the capital within 24 hours. It is reported that the rebels were caught off guard by the militia's sudden and courageous offensive with tanks, aircraft, and armored trains and were forced to retreat. (Reuters Telegram, 30th)

Madrid - The capital city today received its first reports of government forces' victories, and the residents were greatly excited. Furthermore, Prime Minister Caballero's proclamation to the people this morning, expressing the government's determination to resist, received a good impression. Political figures compared today's victory of the government forces to the Battle of the Marne in the European War (Note: In 1915, when the German army pressed on Paris, the French commander Joffre led his troops to resist and defeated the German army at the Marne River, turning the crisis into safety. This was a famous battle in the European War). Today, an armored train also went to the small village of Getafe. In addition, the government forces had secretly prepared several armored trains a few days ago, which were used in the recent fierce attacks on the railway line leading to Ciempozuelos, Alcorcón, and Aranjuez. Government forces are not only launching offensives on the central front but are also reportedly planning to change to offensive operations on other fronts. The concern of the residents of the capital regarding the development of the civil war has now reached its highest point. Wounded soldiers can be seen walking along the streets of the city, most of whom have suffered foot injuries from machine gun bullets and hand grenades. This morning, several government aircraft scattered declarations in the sky over the capital, advising the residents of the capital to join the official army to participate in the great battle to defend the capital. (Havas Telegram, 29th)

Spanish Government Expresses Determination to Resist, Issues Proclamation to the People

Madrid - Prime Minister Caballero issued a proclamation to the people, expressing the government's determination to resist. It was delivered to the troops on the central front this morning, and the commanders gathered the soldiers to read it aloud in public. The text stated: "Since the Fascist traitors marched on the capital, their combat power has been declining day by day, becoming an arrow at the end of its flight. On the government side, the unity is increasing, and powerful mechanized military equipment has been put in place, including tanks and aircraft, without exception. We should take the opportunity to severely wound the traitors. All my comrades, listen to me: at dawn today, our artillery and armored trains will fire first, and the air force will strafe with machine guns. Then, the tank troops will advance and attack the weakest points of the rebel positions. Then, all the soldiers will jump forward, attack the enemy fiercely, and annihilate them. The traitors who lead a small number of troops to their deaths will be punished by public opinion, and our wives and sisters will be rescued from now on. All my comrades, move forward!" After hearing this declaration, the government forces were inspired and launched a major offensive amid shouts of "Never let the traitors pass," successively overcoming the three key towns of Vallecas, Torrejón de Velasco, La Guardia, and Ciempozuelos south of the capital and are now continuing to advance in the direction of Illescas. (Havas Telegram, 29th)

Rebels Propagate Russian Troops Participating in the War

Lisbon - The headquarters of General Varela, commander of the Spanish Nationalist Army, issued a public announcement this morning stating that among the government soldiers captured in the fighting near Madrid yesterday, there were more than 300 Russian soldiers who had recently arrived from Soviet Russia and could not understand a single Spanish word. The announcement also stated that, according to captured government officers, there is now a Soviet Russian general commanding the government forces, concentrating all the troops in the southwest of Madrid, leaving only a very weak outpost force to guard the Guadarrama front. (Reuters Telegram, 30th)

Government Forces Achieve Victory in Offensive on the Northeastern Front, Occupy Huesca

Barcelona - The Catalan Autonomous Government recently announced that government forces entered Huesca yesterday, occupying the lunatic asylum, slaughterhouse, and several large buildings in the city held by the rebels. In addition, government forces also recaptured the two towns of Bumbi and Espa-Pompiros on the Aragon front and occupied part of the city of Jaca. (Havas Telegram, 30th)

Continuous Heavy Rain Obstructs Rebel Advance

Rabat, Morocco - According to a broadcast from the Nationalist Army radio station in the Taza region of Spanish Morocco, continuous heavy rain has delayed the advance of the Nationalist Army columns on Madrid considerably, but there may be more significant news tomorrow. At the same time, the Nationalist Army radio station in Córdoba broadcast an order from Nationalist leader General Franco, ordering all reserve troops to report within five days. (Reuters Telegram, 30th)

Talavera de la Reina - A special dispatch from our correspondent reports that the Nationalist Army expects Madrid to fall in early next week. At that time, the Moroccan indigenous troops will be the first to enter the city from the southwest, occupying the key points of the city center, such as the government offices, radio station, and post office. Then, the tank troops will enter the city, followed slowly by the Moroccan regular army and foreign troops to prevent ambushes. (Havas Telegram, 29th)

Rome Denies Bombarding Spanish Coast

(Rome) - The authorities today formally denied the Spanish government's accusation that Italian warships had bombarded the Catalan coast. (Reuters Telegram, 30th)

No Naval Battle Occurred in Gibraltar

(London) - There were reports of loud cannon fire in the Strait of Gibraltar between Ceuta in Spanish Morocco and Algeciras in Spain, and it was widely believed that it was a fierce battle between warships of the Spanish government forces and the Nationalist Army in the Strait. It is now learned that the cannon fire was due to artillery practice by the Gibraltar forces today. The Gibraltar authorities have formally stated that no naval warfare occurred in the Strait yesterday or today. (Reuters Telegram, 29th)

Britain Maintains Neutrality on the Spanish Civil War, Prevents the Spread of War to All of Europe, Eden's Speech Favors Portugal and Opposes Russia

(London) - During the debate in the House of Commons today on the international situation arising from the Spanish Civil War, Foreign Secretary Eden emphatically stated that the British government would continue to adhere to its policy of non-interference in Spanish affairs, otherwise the situation would inevitably become chaotic, leading to international mutual accusations or perhaps even promoting war. Eden said that this policy has been supported by the majority of the British people. The British people deeply regret the mutual strife and arbitrary killings of the two Spanish parties but believe that the main responsibility of their government is to prevent the spread of the war from the unfortunate country to other countries.

When the House of Commons convened today, the seats for members and the public galleries were full. Many foreign ambassadors and ministers were also present. Prime Minister Baldwin attended the House of Commons for the first time after his illness, his face slightly pale, but he was in good spirits when he finished his speech at the end of the debate.

At the beginning of his speech, Eden detailed the various events before the conclusion of the non-interference agreement, analyzed the effects of the agreement on the two sides, and responded to the accusations regarding the implementation of the agreement. Eden denied rumors that the French government initiated the agreement under pressure from the British government, saying that the French government itself initiated this move. The British government believes that this move is of great help to the peace of Europe. Now, is there anyone who denies that the non-interference policy is the policy that best maintains the peace of Europe? The only point that the House of Commons needs to discuss is this. He knows that the general public believes that the implementation of the agreement is aimed at resisting the Spanish government, and some even say that the agreement has determined the course of the Spanish Civil War. Eden then refuted in detail to prove the fallacy of the various statements, saying that the intention of those who advocated these statements was that without this agreement, the Spanish government could obtain a large amount of foreign arms supplies and eliminate its original disadvantages. Furthermore, before the establishment of the agreement, there was no dispute everywhere, but the Nationalist Army received large amounts of arms supplies from more than one source. The total source of arms supplies for each side was the five countries of Italy, Germany, France, Russia, and Britain. Russia, Italy, and Germany had been manufacturing large quantities of weapons for a long time, making it easy to assist one side they supported with weapons quickly. However, Italy is in an excellent geographical location, so its supply of weapons is more convenient than Russia. As for Britain, due to the needs of its defense procedures, even without the non-interference agreement, the arms that Britain could supply to Spain would not have a significant impact on the outcome of the war. He cannot speak for France, but in the current tense European situation, it is difficult to imagine the difficulty of asking France to supply a large amount of arms. Therefore, he would like to ask the members who believe that the implementation of the non-interference agreement is completely unfavorable to the Spanish government to reconsider this matter and contemplate the debate he has just made. The Foreign Secretary continued to mention the implementation of the agreement and the International Committee, saying that the British government had done its best to make the committee effective and expedite all discussions. The British representative even proposed a proposal to monitor the land and sea entry points of Spain at yesterday's meeting of the committee. The Foreign Secretary then criticized Russia's attitude towards Portugal, saying that the British government had never supported Russia's proposal to monitor Portuguese ports. Now, in fairness, the various information received by the British government has not proven that Portugal has violated the non-interference agreement.

The Foreign Secretary then informed the House of Commons that the British government will continue to maintain close contact with the French government, hoping to jointly decide everything because both democratic governments bear important responsibilities. Eden then praised the British Navy, which had transported 6,000 refugees from Spain, including 2,000 British nationals. Many foreign governments have sent letters of thanks.

After the Foreign Secretary's speech, Labour Party member Greenwood and Liberal Party leader Sinclair both requested clarification of the truth about the Balearic Islands, as it was rumored that Italian troops had now taken control of the islands. Greenwood said that Gibraltar is now smiling at the Spanish Fascists and frowning at those loyal to the Spanish government. Sinclair said that the Spanish Fascist Party could not succeed without the assistance of Italy, which must have been agreed upon in advance. Sinclair advocated maintaining the non-interference agreement, saying that if France or Britain supplied one cannon to Spain, Italy and Germany could supply fifty cannons, so it is still advisable to maintain the non-interference agreement.

Prime Minister Baldwin made a speech to end the debate, saying that both sides had inevitably violated the non-interference agreement to some extent, but its importance was not enough to make Britain revise its policy. Since the end of August, Britain has continued to promote its humanitarian efforts in Spain. The British government had exchanged hostages with the Spanish government but was rejected, so it later made this proposal to the Burgos authorities. However, the British government has been doing everything alone, and it has been quite effective. The British representative in Madrid, together with the diplomatic corps, privately asked the Spanish government to curb private feuds and place reliable guards in various prisons. Now, the Spanish authorities have given assurances that all killings will be stopped, and the beautiful results of the appeals from all parties will be immediately visible.

Baldwin continued, saying that as far as Britain is concerned, both the communist and fascist forces have no way to exercise their skills, and we should thank God for this. He believes that the difference between democratic and autocratic political systems lies in the fact that the former publishes all its troubles to the world, while under autocracy, we must speculate on where its troubles lie. Baldwin further said, "The British political system is relatively sound. Although there are differences of opinion between Sir Nevile Henderson and the Air Ministry, the scope is also very small. The outside world has been exaggerating and it is not the truth." Baldwin spared no effort in criticizing both communism and fascism, continuing to say that some people believe that Germany may attack Britain one day, saying that Britain's danger is not in Germany. He believes that there is no reason why the tragedy of war cannot be avoided.

Baldwin concluded, "What we are working hard to do now is world peace." (Reuters Telegram, 29th)

Turkey Abolishes: Trade Agreement with Japan.

(Tokyo) According to an official telegram received by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 29th, the Turkish government notified Miyazaki, the acting ambassador stationed in Turkey, in a document dated the 28th, that it was abolishing the provisional Japan-Turkey trade agreement. Therefore, this agreement will expire on January 2nd of next year. However, the Turkish government stated that it was prepared to begin discussing the fundamental issues regarding the establishment of a new treaty with Japan. The provisional Japan-Turkey trade agreement was signed on December 22nd, Showa 9 (1934), stipulating that both countries could export goods worth up to 4 million Turkish lira with a compensatory nature. However, the compensatory affairs could not proceed smoothly afterward. Japan purchased Turkish goods and the Franco-Turkish treaty expired. Japanese cotton cloth became subject to high tariffs. The Japanese side also intended to revise the agreement. Therefore, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs plans to instruct Acting Ambassador Miyazaki to begin negotiations with the Turkish government in early November. (30th Domei dispatch)

Bloodless Coup in Iraq: Successful Overthrow of Yasin Cabinet.

(London) A violent but bloodless coup d'état took place yesterday in Baghdad, the capital of Iraq, forcing Prime Minister General Yasin to resign. The news only reached London today, more than twenty-four hours after the event. According to the Foreign Office, Prime Minister General Yasin, fearing the use of force and inevitable bloodshed, submitted his resignation at 1:00 PM yesterday. The King then ordered Mr. Salih to form a new cabinet. Baghdad is calm, but details of the coup have not been disclosed.

According to private sources, the coup was organized by Mr. Sitki, a leader of the Ghult tribe. Initially, airplanes flew over Baghdad, dropping pamphlets demanding the government's resignation. Two hours later, the planes returned and bombed government offices. Prime Minister Yasin then entered the palace and resigned. The new cabinet formed by Salih was subsequently announced. (30th Reuters dispatch)

(London) According to observers, the outcome of this coup in Iraq may have far-reaching implications for the Middle East. In 1933, he joined the cabinet, but the cabinet dissolved after the revolt of the Kawdish tribe in the central Euphrates region, and Salih also resigned. (30th Reuters dispatch)

San Francisco: Seamen's Strike: 35,000 Participants: Pacific Shipping Suspended.

San Francisco: 35,000 members of the Seafarers International Union began a general strike at midnight last night, causing Pacific shipping to be suspended. The labor-management conflict in the shipping industry of 1934 is about to reignite. A total of 300 ships are currently unable to set sail. Sailors, engineers, and radio operators were ordered to leave their ships and go ashore at 00:30 this morning, flocking to the union headquarters to prepare for picket duty. The strike order was issued by the seven Seafarers International Union Joint Negotiating Committee via telegram to ports such as Seattle, Portland, and San Pedro at midnight. A strike action committee has now been formed. Labor Secretary McGrady announced somberly after hearing the news that this was a major failure of his initial efforts to mediate the labor dispute. Strike committee spokesperson Molly Levitch declared that unions across the country have wired their support for our strike movement. Local police authorities have dispatched an additional 392 police officers to maintain order in the dock area. (30th Kuomintang dispatch)

France Expands Navy: Adds 51 New Ships: Submarines Occupy Important Position.

(Paris) Well-informed sources recently stated that the 1937 naval construction plan proposed by Navy Minister Gasnier has been approved by the cabinet. The plan advocates the construction of 51 new ships, totaling 47,000 tons, including one 8,000-ton cruiser, two 1,850-ton destroyers, a number of 1,000-ton destroyers, three 1,500-ton submarines, two small submarines, two special submarines, 28 small gunboats, a number of submarine destroyers, four aircraft carrier transport ships, two colonial patrol aircraft, two torpedo transport ships, and one oil tanker. As for the main battleship category, there are already four ships under construction, two with 35,000 tons and two with 26,500 tons. Once they are completed, they will be sufficient for deployment, so it is not planned to add more in the next year. In addition, there are six 7,200-ton cruisers that can be completed and incorporated into the fleet, and there are also 32 2,000-ton destroyers, so it is not planned to add more. However, certain types of destroyers, which have been suspended since 1926, must be rebuilt. From the above, it is clear that submarines are still the most important category. However, considering the characteristics of the 1937 naval construction plan, the number of small ships is also relatively large, which goes without saying. Regarding this plan, the Petit Parisien newspaper recently published a commentary, saying, "This plan can be called transitional. Its purpose is to supplement the insufficient number of small ships belonging to the French fleet, and then, within a short period of time, to propose a new plan advocating the construction of two 8,000-ton cruisers and one or two aircraft carriers." (30th Havas dispatch)
