Overview of Shanghai Municipal Council Elementary Schools (1) Special Dispatch from This Newspaper Investigation by Hu Zuyin

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession has established six Chinese elementary day schools and two night schools within the concession, with a total of 4,886 students. This article will provide a brief introduction to the various facilities of the Chinese elementary day schools and night schools established by the Municipal Council. As for the various facilities of the Western Public School and Chinese Middle School established by the Municipal Council, they are not within the scope of this article and will be temporarily omitted. The author is grateful to Mr. Chen Heqin, Director of the Chinese Education Department of the Municipal Council, for his guidance, and to the principals of the Chinese elementary day schools and the directors of the night schools for providing materials.

1. History of School Establishment

The Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council established Chinese elementary schools starting on October 8, 1928. The Municipal Council had already established four Chinese middle schools in the concession, but Chinese elementary schools had not yet been opened. Mr. Yu Qiaqing and other Chinese directors, in view of the large number of young school-age children in the concession, proposed at the initial meeting of the Public Concession Board of Directors that more Chinese elementary schools should be established in the concession, and that they should be managed by Chinese. After detailed discussion by the Municipal Council Board of Directors, it was approved that two Chinese elementary schools should be established on a trial basis by the Chinese first, and Mr. Chen Heqin, an expert in children's education, was hired as the Director of the Chinese Education Department of the Municipal Council to preside over Chinese education in the concession.

On October 8, 1928, the Municipal Council officially opened the Eastern District and Northern District Chinese elementary schools: the Eastern District Elementary School was located at No. 150 Huishan Road; the Northern District Elementary School was located at No. 228 Bagan Road. Both schools rented Western-style residences. Initially, the two schools had a total of only 165 students. In September 1930, the Northern District Elementary School on Bagan Road moved into the Chinese Public School building on Kenning Road. (Because the Chinese Public School had a larger school building elsewhere) From then on, the Northern District Elementary School had a formal school building. In September of the same year, the Municipal Council rented a civil house at No. 914 Avenue Road in the Western District and opened a Western District Elementary School. At this time, the number of Chinese elementary schools had increased to three: the number of students had also increased to 1,147.

2. Eight-Year Education Plan

In order to plan and improve the educational facilities in the concession, the Municipal Council established a School Affairs Committee on June 18, 1930. The committee had a total of nine members, and the Chinese members who participated successively included Mr. Liu Zhanen, Ou Yuanhuai, Yuan Ludeng, Lin Kanghou, Chen Zheqing, and Xi Yushu. The committee suggested to the Municipal Council in 1931 that an eight-year education plan be implemented. This education plan was formally approved by the Municipal Council Board of Directors, but it was reserved for reconsideration at the end of 1934. The aspects of the eight-year education plan related to the expansion and improvement of Chinese education included: (1) From 1931 to 1938, two Chinese elementary schools for both boys and girls should be added each year, each accommodating 600 students. (2) One Chinese girls' middle school should be added in 1931; another Chinese girls' middle school should be added before the end of 1934. (3) The existing four Chinese Public Schools should be gradually converted into more definitive middle schools, in line with the middle school system promulgated by the Chinese government. (4) The principals, administrative staff, and teachers of Chinese middle schools should, as far as possible, be replaced by competent Chinese personnel. (5) Private Chinese elementary and middle schools in the concession that are well-managed may request financial assistance from the Municipal Council.

According to the above education plan, the Municipal Council rented a civil house at No. 233 Meadow Road on September 9, 1931, and opened a Chinese girls' middle school. In April 1932, it rented the original school building of the Zhaoshangju Public School on Huade Road and opened a Huade Road Chinese elementary school. In September 1932, a new Chinese elementary school building was completed on Xinzha Road; the students of the Western District Elementary School, which was originally studying on Avenue Road, formally moved into the new school building for classes. In February 1933, a new school building was completed on Jingzhou Road; it officially started enrolling students on March 1 of the same year. At this time, the Municipal Council also purchased the Huishan Road Eastern District Elementary School building and converted it into the Eastern District Girls' Elementary School building; the newly opened Jingzhou Road Elementary School was converted into the Eastern District Boys' Elementary School. The Huade Road Elementary School was a co-educational elementary school for both boys and girls in the Eastern District. Regarding the third, fourth and fifth points, the Municipal Council also made efforts to implement them within a considerable range, which will not be repeated here. At that time, the world was in a state of depression, and the Shanghai Public Concession was also deeply affected. The Municipal Council's various tax revenues decreased sharply; therefore, at the end of 1934, the Municipal Council Board of Directors reconsidered the eight-year education plan proposed by the School Affairs Committee and temporarily suspended its implementation. As a result, the plan to add two Chinese elementary schools each year was not fully realized.

In October 1935, the Municipal Council opened a Jingzhou Road night school in the Lizhou Road Elementary School building, enrolling male workers who worked in factories and had not completed elementary school. In February of this year, it opened a Huishan Road night school in the Huishan Road Eastern District Girls' Elementary School building, enrolling female workers who worked in factories and had not completed elementary school. In April of this year, it added a two-part Chinese elementary school at the original site of the Road Western Public School. To date, the Municipal Council has opened six Chinese elementary day schools and two night schools in the concession. The names, addresses, and establishment dates of the eight schools are surveyed and copied below:

Survey Table of the Names, Addresses, and Establishment Dates of Shanghai Municipal Council Elementary Schools (Surveyed in July 1936)

The Children's Welfare Association Held its Second Plenary Meeting

Planning to establish a shelter for homeless children and a receiving center for destitute children, taking over the labor nursery, and continuing to manage the city's children's welfare undertaking. The committee of the Municipal Children's Welfare Undertaking held its second plenary meeting yesterday at the Social Affairs Bureau. Committee members Zhang Binghui, Jiang Jianbai, Hu Shuyi, Yin Guanzhi, Sun Yongyi, Feng Liutang, Qian Fugong, Lei Kenan, Yan Wenkai, Wang Gang, Zou Lieguang, Shen Duo, and others attended. Zhang Binghui presided over the meeting, and Guo Junshi recorded the minutes. First, the chairman reported: (1) According to the order of the Social Affairs Bureau, this association will take over the Children's Welfare Association, and the nurseries run by the association will also be transferred to this association; (2) The Standing Committee decided to invite Committee Member Sun Yongyi to serve concurrently as the director-general of this association. The candidates for staff will be submitted by the director-general to the Standing Committee for appointment. Then, the following items were discussed: (1) The merger of the Social Education Bureau and the Education Bureau, and the proposed amendment to Article 4, Item A of the association's charter. It was resolved to first request the bureau chief to determine the number of representatives and candidates from the two bureaus, and then submit it to the municipal government for amendment; (2) Whether to continue running the nursery, please make a public decision. It was resolved to continue running the nursery; (3) How to handle the unreceived funds of the Children's Welfare Association. It was resolved to recommend Committee Member Hu Shuyi to go to the Finance Bureau with Mr. Song Yaochen to discuss and receive the funds; (4) Outline of the association's business plan. It was resolved to adopt the proposal of Committee Member Sun after amendment, to establish a shelter for homeless children and destitute children, with an estimated start-up cost of 10,000 yuan and a monthly recurring cost of 10,000 yuan, and to submit a separate budget to the government for approval and appropriation. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Notifies Public and Private Middle Schools

Purchase the "Modern High School Composition Essence" and "Modern Junior High School Composition Essence" published by the Diligent Bookstore, No. 392 Laozhaoshenfu Road. These two books are collections of selected student compositions from over 4,000 middle schools across the country. The education authorities have unanimously praised them. After reading these books, students can expand their writing ideas, broaden their minds, and study the works of others, which will increase their own thoughts and writing skills. The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has issued Order No. 425 to the city's private middle schools to purchase these books. The original order is recorded as follows: "According to the report of the Diligent Bookstore, No. 392 Laozhaoshenfu Road, 'The Bureau believes that middle school students are the backbone of society, and the Chinese language course is the foundation of all courses. Whether it is in terms of individuals or society, it will affect the entire nation and country in the future. Therefore, during the middle school period, the writing skills of composition must be rigorously practiced in order to express ideas clearly and accurately, so that they can further their studies and research various academic subjects, and can retreat to apply practical knowledge and serve society. Otherwise, if the foundation is not solid, they will lose their way, and in recent years, middle school students have neglected basic literature and art because of their research in science, resulting in poor performance and difficulty in mastering various subjects. If they want to further their studies in various academic subjects, they must first work hard, explore literature and art, practice writing, and demand an increase in writing ability. Although there is more than one way, reading appropriate works is the most important. Although there are many publications on the market, they are either lengthy works or have complex ideas, which are not suitable for middle school students to read. In the past, although there were publications of student achievements, the themes were limited to classics and history, and the ideas tended to be outdated, which is not what is needed in the current era of rapid production and construction. Moreover, there is no object of comparison, and if they are allowed to explore blindly, progress will be slow. In response to this need, the Bureau has collected student composition achievements from public and private high schools and junior high schools in various provinces and cities across the country, spending six months, edited by Ma Chonggan, and reviewed by experts Hu Pu'an, He Shuangqiu, Xie Engao, and others. Based on the Chinese language curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education, we have selected the National Modern High School Composition Essence and the National Modern Junior High School Composition Essence, each in four volumes. The content is divided into thirteen categories, and the themes include the universe, insects, and the construction of national revival. This is a textbook for middle school students to study on their own after class, to compare and contrast themselves, and to supplement the deficiencies of the Chinese language textbook, promote writing skills, and is necessary for general middle school students. We respectfully attach a copy of each book for your review and request your approval to notify all public and private high schools and junior high schools in the city to consider purchasing them and inform students to purchase them to promote and value culture, which is a great public benefit.' According to this, the selection standards of the two books, National Modern High School Composition Essence and National Modern Junior High School Composition Essence, published by the bookstore, are still practical. If the schools need them, they can consider purchasing them. In addition to the approval and separate orders, the school is hereby ordered to be informed. This order is issued by Director Pan Gongzhan on October 16, 1936. The special price for the two books is 1.7 yuan each, and the special price for purchasing any two books together is 3 yuan. The registered postage for each book is 16 cents. The bookstore's retail department at No. 277 Sima Road in this city also sells them at the same price."

Shanghai Secondary School Association Meeting

The Shanghai Secondary School Association, established by various renowned secondary schools in the city, has reached its eighth year. Aside from discussing common issues among the schools, it also holds periodic academic lectures on various subjects and mutual visits. It has greatly promoted the improvement of secondary education in the city. Recently, the association held its 57th general meeting at the Kung Teh Lin Vegetarian Restaurant. More than twenty people attended, including school principals Liao Mao-ru, Shen Ti-lan, Sun Kang-zeng, Cheng Kuan-zheng, and Tao Guang-chuan. Zheng Xi-gu chaired the meeting, and Wu Cui-lun served as the recorder. In addition to reporting on the association's affairs and financial situation, the following resolutions were passed: (1) to organize a lecture group to give speeches in various locations to stimulate public morale; (2) to hold a mathematics discussion to increase the effectiveness of mathematics education; (3) to suggest that the Social Affairs Bureau assist in providing specialized education that individual schools find difficult to handle alone; (4) to have Shen Ti-lan, Tao Guang-chuan, and Jia Fo-ru consult with the Military Training Association and the Social Affairs Bureau on methods for organizing military training teams; (5) to approve the New Universe Vocational School's membership; (6) to replace Hong Kong Provincial Shanghai High School, Guanghua Affiliated High School, Chinese Vocational School, Datong University Affiliated High School, and Fudan Affiliated High School with Wu Song, Ren Lun, Jing Ye and Er Xiao Schools as standing committee members and alternates. Furthermore, the association held a standing committee meeting yesterday at the YMCA, resolving: (1) to hold the mathematics discussion on November 18th at the East Hall on the ninth floor of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA, soliciting topics from various schools and assigning Shanghai High School and Guanghua School to be responsible for organizing them; (2) to organize a lecture group, appointing Zheng Xi-gu, Liao Mao-ru, Sun Kang-zeng, Yin Yi-wen, and Shen Ti-lan as speakers, with the topic set as "Youth and the Nation," and tasking Zheng Xi-gu and Liao Mao-ru with drafting an outline, first lecturing at member schools of the association and then giving public speeches to stimulate public morale; (3) to request the Social Affairs Bureau to assist in implementing special education, such as providing anti-gas equipment, military lectures, and military drills. As for the association's previously solicited morning assembly song, it has reportedly been sent to Cheng Mao-yun for composition.

The Ministry of Education yesterday released statistics comparing the accumulated value of newly added equipment in national colleges and universities over the past few years, as follows:

(Explanation) (1) The terms A, B, and C each represent value, accumulated value over the years, and multiple of accumulated value over the years. All values are in units of one thousand yuan. For example, A value of 81 for health equipment means 81,000 yuan. The rest can be inferred similarly. Also, a multiple of 1.00 means one time, and 1.99 means one time plus 99% of a fraction, less than two times. The rest can be inferred similarly. (2) The value of school equipment for the 20th year (of the Republic) is 923,000 yuan, including health equipment. The expenditure on health equipment for that year was not analyzed separately. (3) In terms of the average percentage of each item, health equipment accounts for 1.83%, school equipment accounts for 15.33%, books account for 17.54%, instruments and machines account for 28.49%, and building repairs account for 36.81%.

Hangzhou Art Academy Volleyball Team Visits Shanghai - Winning the First Battle, Slightly Defeating Chi Chee University - Chi Chee University's Efforts Fall Short at Three to Two

The National Hangzhou Art Academy volleyball team has been the champion team in Hangzhou for many years. Recently, it surpassed its strong rival Aviation Team in the same city to win the Martyr's Cup Championship for the 25th year (of the Republic). Most of the team members, such as Zhao Yun-xiu, Zhao Chong-huo, and He Shu-sheng, are famous players from the National Games. This season, new players Mo Gui-xin and Wei Zhi-yang have been added, making the team even more formidable. The team, led by team leader Mr. Li Xin-biao, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning for sightseeing. Yesterday afternoon, they played a friendly match with the strong Chi Chee University team at the university's court. The two powerful teams met, resulting in a fiercely contested match. After the exchange, the Art Academy was sharp and aggressive, with flexible coordination between the front and back rows, taking the lead with a score of 21 to 11. In the second and third games, Chi Chee University refused to give in, with the forwards and guards shouting in unison, quickly winning with two scores of 21 to 18, reversing the situation to two to one and gaining the upper hand. All that was needed was to win one more game to secure the final victory. Both sides were attacking and defending, making it difficult to break the deadlock. However, the Art Academy's forwards Wei and Zhao were skilled in spiking and pressing, their attacks as sharp as cannonballs. He Shu-yun coordinated in the center, making every shot count, and they managed to win back the fourth game with a score of 21 to 12, resulting in a tie. The final decisive game was particularly tense, with both sides putting everything on the line, unwilling to give an inch. Chi Chee University had the right to change sides first, giving them a superior position. Unexpectedly, the Art Academy launched a surprise attack, catching the home team off guard, and quickly took the lead with a score of 21 to 16, securing the final victory. The overall result was three to two, with Chi Chee suffering a slight defeat. The lineups were as follows:

Business News

Finance - Pure Gold Downstream - Gold Standard Also Weak Yesterday

The gold market was still weak yesterday due to downstream pure gold. However, sentiment has stabilized, and the market situation is still calm. Industry players are uninterested, and the overall trend is becoming more stagnant. In the early morning, overseas silver markets showed London up and the U.S. flat. Monte Carlo forward silver prices rose by two to three points. Exchange rates slightly contracted. London raw gold fell by half a penny. The Central Bank's official exchange rate announcement showed both the British and U.S. rates flat. The Customs Gold Unit remained unchanged. The gold standard price dropped to 1,155 yuan and 70 cents. The morning opening was slightly lower, but stabilized after the opening. However, it is still difficult for the bulls to be optimistic, and there was some selling at higher prices. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's official exchange rate announcement showed the British rate up by 0.03125, while the U.S. rate was flat. Gradually turned lower. The Silver Equalization Tax announcement showed a rise of half a point. Subsequent trading was sparse, with major fluctuations and the situation quite unstable. The market situation was even more stagnant, with industry players uninterested and few willing to take action. Although there was a slight pull-up in the middle, physical gold sellers were eager to sell, and in the end, it was still difficult to be optimistic. However, the trend is still stable. The swap premium unexpectedly rose to four yuan for the bull side to pay out. The market situation for the day is recorded below:

The morning opening was 1,154 yuan and 30 cents, a drop of 20 cents compared to the previous close. Dadecheng, Qiafeng, Yongqian, Changxiang bought bars, rising to 4 yuan and 90 cents. Fuyu sold. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's official exchange rate announcement showed the British rate up by 0.03125, while the U.S. dollar was flat, gradually moving downstream. The Silver Equalization Tax rose by half a point, but then fell to 4 yuan and 40 cents. Hengyu once reached 4 yuan and 80 cents. Jingfu and Dadecheng still sold, then fell to 4 yuan and 40 cents. Qiafeng, Yonghongli, and others bought slightly and then turned to sideways trading. The noon close was 1,154 yuan and 50 cents.

The afternoon market opened at 1,154 yuan and 50 cents. Tongfeng, Hengjiu, Dayuanmao, Yongdeng, and others bought slightly, rising to 4 yuan and 70 cents. Dafengheng seized the opportunity to sell. The closing price fell to 1,154 yuan and 40 cents.

The closing price was announced by the Central Bank at a standard gold price of 1,155 yuan and 70 cents, a loss of more than 1 yuan based on the closing price. November registration was 1,153 yuan, and December was 1,155 yuan. The morning water top-up was 251 yuan. The physical market situation was calm. Physical gold was sold by Taikangrun for 140 taels and by Jingfu for 100 taels, priced at 13 yuan more, purchased by silver shops and the Hankou gang. The buying price was 8 yuan more, and Tianjin goods were 11.5 yuan more, but there were no transactions. Due to physical gold congestion, and because the next month is the end of the year, it is predicted that the next issue premium will be more expensive. The bulls are eager to pay out, and it has risen to 4 yuan. Dadecheng paid Futaiheng eleven bars, and in the afternoon, Dafengheng paid Yiyu fourteen bars at 3.5 yuan, and Chengda paid Shengyuan Yong forty-nine bars at 3.6 yuan.

The volume of transactions in the market was limited. In summary, Qiafeng, Yongfuxing, Yonghengyu, Tongfeng, Hengjiu, and Da were on the buying side, while Dadecheng, Yuanmao, Yongjingfu, Yingfengheng, Fuyudafengheng, and Shen Dayong were on the selling side. Chengda划于Shengyuan Yong 350 bars, priced at 44 yuan and 60 cents. Hengyu went in first and then out, and Yuanmao and Yong went out first and then in.

The market situation for the day was peaceful. The morning opening was 1,154 yuan and 30 cents, and the closing was 1,154 yuan and 40 cents. The highest price was 1,154 yuan and 90 cents, and the lowest price was 1,154 yuan and 30 cents, with a fluctuation of only 60 cents. The result was a slight drop of 10 cents compared to the previous close. There were 2,233 November short term deals remaining, with a total of five long parties and twelve short parties. There were 6,433 December chips, with a total of 37 bull parties and 26 bear parties. The total number of transactions was 805 in the morning and 389 in the afternoon.

Chinese Merchants Dumping, British and American Exchange Rates Turn Loose

British American Tobacco Still Buying, Swap Prices Also Tighten

The exchange market was soft yesterday due to Chinese merchants dumping and short covering, causing British and American exchange rates to weaken. In the early morning, overseas telegrams reported large increases in London, both near and far, of 0.0625. The report said that the market participants were satisfied after the close, and the silver market rose further. Monte Carlo forward silver prices rose by 2 to 3 points. London raw gold fell by half a penny, the British rate against the US rate fell by .0125. The British rate against the French rate rose by 3 points. The US rate against the British rate fell by 0.0625, and the US rate against the French rate fell by 3.75. The Central Bank's official exchange rate announcement showed both the British and American rates flat. The Customs Gold Unit remained unchanged. The exchange market's morning opening saw recent selling prices with the British rate at 1 shilling 2 and 46875/100000 pence against a half penny up, and the American rate at 29 yuan and a half and 5625/10000 against a half penny up, with both the British and American rates flat compared to the previous close. After the opening, Chinese merchants slightly reduced the amount of shillings, and foreign banks also supplied more than they demanded. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's official exchange rate announcement showed the British rate up by 0.03125, while the US dollar was flat. Although Chinese traders came to maintain the rate, the trend was still difficult to support. Later, British American Tobacco stepped in to conclude the settlements, and the Silver Equalization Tax also rose by half a point, and then began to hover. In the afternoon, Chinese merchants still slightly sold out shillings, and Japanese banks dumped US dollars. Foreign banks were still buying, and the only change was the short covering of swaps. The Indian silver rate rose by one anna, with no further changes. At the close, the current British rate was 1 shilling 2 and a half pence, and the American rate was 29 yuan and 52225/100000, with the American rate flat and the British rate slightly looser compared to the previous close. The forward rates saw the British rate loosen by 0.0625 and the American rate strengthen by 0.09375. The day's transactions are recorded below:

As for the British exchange rate, recent selling prices were heard in the morning at 1 shilling 2 and 46875/100000 pence against a half penny up. Hua Bi bought from Citi and Hong Kong and Shanghai, and Mai Jia bought from British American Tobacco, spot half penny. For the American exchange rate, the opening was 29 yuan and a half and 5625/10000 against a half penny up. Zhejiang Da bought a December 4375/10000. Dongfang sold to Mai Jiahe Citi a spot 5625/10000. Securities - Both Long and Short Positions Wait and See in the Bond Market

Yesterday, although the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange resumed trading after being closed for a day, the market situation still hovered without much rise or fall. In general, it has not yet escaped the brewing stage. It is difficult to predict whether there will be any changes in the future. Both the long and short positions have their own reasons for observing, so they are observing each other, and the situation is even more stagnant. Before Sino-Japanese diplomacy can be opened up, the market price will likely not develop easily. Yesterday's progress: In the morning, the type C bonds opened slightly firm, but later the selling pressure was slightly stronger, and the subsequent ones all saw weakness, falling by a small 5/100th to 2.5/100ths of a yuan. In the closing session, retail investors sold, which was relatively lively, and then fell by another 5/100ths to 2/100ths of a yuan. In the afternoon opening, the 32nd and 35th numbers saw quite a bit of selling, and the type C quick delivery fell by 0.3 yuan, while the rest also fell by a small 5/100ths to 2/100ths of a yuan. Only the type A forward contracts were good by 0.1 yuan. At the close, scattered retail investors bought, and the table rose while the shorts covered their positions. Although the type C continued to fall slightly by about 0.1 yuan, the rest all rose slightly by 5/100ths to 2/100ths of a yuan. As a result, the market price was slightly better for the type A of this month by 5/100ths of a yuan, while the rest all fell slightly by 5/100ths to 0.3 yuan. The total turnover was 4,315,000 yuan. Amidst Cheerful Yarn Sales, Stocks of Chinese and Foreign Yarn Mills Surge

Recently, cotton yarn sales have surged, and various yarn mills are unable to meet the demand, with a hectic pace of business. Operations have improved, and profits are very high. The stock market naturally began to buy stocks of yarn mills. Stock prices rose sharply. The old stocks of Shanghai Japanese yarn mills rose by 20%, and the new stocks rose by 30%. The stocks of the British-owned Ewo Yarns soared. Chinese yarn mill stocks also rose, but Chinese mill stocks are not publicly traded, so trading is reduced. The price increase is also about 20%.

Women's Special Issue

Cotton Yarn October Cotton Yarn Settlement Overview and Process Yarn Price Soars, Peak Reaching 240 Yuan Settlement Amount Totals 7,550 Bales Cotton Price Hits High of 43.60 Yuan Amount Reaches 113,400 Dan

Yarn: The October contract of Yu Ji Brand Yarn started at 203 yuan on September 1st of this year, showing a slight increase. Following the announcement of the Sino-British currency issue, public sentiment became uneasy. Coupled with rampant smuggling in North China and sluggish real demand, bearish forces seized the opportunity to become highly active, with heavy selling pressure. Market prices plummeted, breaking the 200 yuan mark in mid-month, reaching a low of 196.10 yuan. Subsequently, due to vigorous buying from certain quarters, rumors of the issuance of circulating notes, and a general surge in overseas yarn and cotton prices, short sellers rushed to cover their positions, and market prices rebounded. By early July, estimates of American cotton yields surged by 60 points, further boosting market confidence, and prices advanced, reaching a peak of 219.80 yuan. Subsequently, due to abundant cotton production in our country, cotton prices declined, selling pressure resurfaced, and financial sentiment shifted from bullish to bearish, returning to 196 yuan. In the most recent two months, due to the development of yarn sales and brisk purchasing by various merchant groups, almost all 30,000 bales of spot goods in yarn and cloth warehouses were swept away. Factories reported yarn shortages, and market prices rose steadily. Short sellers became greatly alarmed, with the highest price reaching 240 yuan, marking a new high in five years. The closing price was 211.11 yuan, an increase of 28 yuan from the opening price. As a result, 7,550 bales remained, an increase of 1,200 bales compared to the previous month. The settlement price for the last three days was averaged at 236 yuan, a sharp increase of 35 yuan compared to the previous month. The delivered goods included 450 bales of new 20-count Jincheng yarn, 200 bales of Shuanglu yarn, 50 bales of Jinta yarn, and the remainder being old stocks. The brokerage firms and quantities involved in the delivery between the buying and selling parties are recorded below:

Selling Party of Marked Yarn

Changji 100, Chengji 200, Tongji 450, Yuda 200

Daji 50, Penji 100, Zhenda 100, Tai 400

Hengde 50, Ren 50, Yuanyi 500, Taichang 50

Runlian 450

Buying Party of Marked Yarn

Yukang 200, Da 100, Gengxin 400, Chang 3800

Cotton: The October cotton contract opened at 41.15 yuan on May 1st of this year. At that time, due to the good yarn market, prices rebounded after falling, struggling around the 40 yuan mark for a long time. On July 8th, the estimate of American cotton fields was released, jumping 60 points, and market sentiment soared, rising to 43.10 yuan. Subsequently, on August 20th, the estimate of cotton production in our country was released, indicating a bumper harvest, with the national output exceeding 16.1 million dan. The market was shaken, and selling pressure was strong. At the same time, the banking sector shifted from bullish to bearish with large volumes. Market prices plummeted, with the low reaching 36.85 yuan. Recently, due to the improvement in yarn sales, the amount of short selling was said to be difficult to fulfill. Prices soared by more than 2 yuan in one day, with the peak reaching 43.60 yuan. A day later, due to the authorities' efforts, the settlement was expected to be resolved. Prices plunged 1.5 yuan to close at 40.07 yuan. As a result, 113,400 dan remained. The settlement price for the three days was averaged at 41 yuan. The delivered goods included Chen Zu Rong, Taicang cotton, Huoji cotton, Shaanxi cotton, Shashi cotton, and Lingshi cotton. New American Cotton Sales Greatly Reduced

Yesterday, the American cotton market opened with sluggish conditions. Prices for various months fell by two points to rise by one point. Industry players and foreign merchants bought in, but short selling continued to increase. New sales were greatly reduced, and most industry players remained on the sidelines. Real demand was relatively quiet, and the footing was still solid. The cloth market was firm but stagnant. Some short covering occurred at the close, stabilizing the market to some extent. Spot prices fell by one point, while futures prices fell by one to five points. British cotton spot prices fell by seven points, while futures prices fell by one to four points. Indian cotton was initially weak due to long liquidation, but then firmed due to short covering by some and buying by industry players. However, it softened again due to selling by brokers. Pingguoer fell by 0.25 rupees, Aomula rose by 0.5 to 1 rupee, and Bailuoxi remained unchanged, according to the original telegram. (Telegram of the 29th)

According to a Mumbai telegram, the opening forecast for the 30th was: Bailuoxi at 218 rupees, down 0.75 rupees; Aomula at 195.5 rupees, down 1 rupee; and Pingguoer at 157 rupees, down 0.75 rupees.

Piece Goods Factory Fine Cloths Due on the Expiry Date Trading Houses Quite a Few Selling Off at Reduced Prices

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market was quiet due to the marked yarn and cotton settlements. Moreover, as the end of the month approached, most trading houses had ordered fine cloths from Japanese factories for this month. According to Japanese factories' usual practice, even without spot goods, they must all be delivered. Therefore, those who thought the price would fall secretly reduced prices, and quite a few were selling off. The market was chaotic, but the factories had no intention of lowering prices, so most who held goods were prepared to put up money and wait for next month's market. Moreover, the remaining amount for the month was not much. Customers and merchants on this street lacked the intention to buy, only urging to finalize orders. Currently, cloth factories have many orders and are not delivering. However, due to the yarn and thread shortage that affected them weeks ago, the number of deliveries was greatly reduced, causing delays and resulting in huge outstanding orders. This factory's coarse cloths rose too quickly weeks ago, reaching as high as 2.3 yuan. Although they are gradually falling back now, it is still difficult to stabilize. Yesterday, each factory's heavy coarse cloths still fell by 1 to 2 jiao. The market for colored goods such as oblique blue cloth, Zhigong Serge, crepe and printed goods was soft, and selling prices had not yet changed. Only white flannel, double-sided flannel and colored striped flannel continued to sell well, with shortages of spot goods, making them the most popular.

Western Suit Fabrics (Shameen) are Even More Popular

Shameen has been selling well recently. Tailor shops of local merchants on this street all need to purchase it because customers who order custom-made Western suits from door shops all specifically choose it. However, most of what is currently in the market is lower-grade domestic goods priced at 4 to 5 yuan per yard. The higher-grade, plain gray, solid color Western suit fabrics priced at 7 to 8 yuan per yard are quite scarce. Therefore, brokers have been busy running the streets to search for them recently. Although the quantity is not large, the atmosphere has become tighter, and prices have risen accordingly. Yesterday, genuine first-grade Shameen was being sold by retailers at 12 yuan per yard, and ordinary Shameen was being sold at 8.75 yuan.

Food Flour Slightly Set Back by Foreign Wheat

Yesterday, the flour market showed a downward trend in all months after the opening of the market in the morning. This was because the price of foreign wheat was reported to be falling, with Chicago down 2 to 3 jiao, Canada down about 7 jiao, and Liverpool down 1 to 2 pence. Therefore, when prices opened, people felt very uneasy, and near and far month prices immediately fell by about 2 fen. Moreover, there was talk that the Tianjin Exchange would hold regular auctions. After that, there would likely be competition, so there was very little trading after the market opened, and prices were slightly flat. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading was busier, and the market rose slightly. People in the industry thought that although the price of foreign wheat had fallen, the price was still not close, so they resisted very strongly. According to this trend, perhaps if the rumored tax exemption on foreign wheat gives factories ample stock to dump, then people will easily comply.

Australian Wheat May Be Exported Futures Wheat Is Difficult to Rally

Yesterday's futures wheat market saw prices fall in all months when the market opened in the morning. This was because the price of foreign wheat was reported to be falling sharply, and it was rumored that Australian wheat could be exported, and prices were easing, which was not without reason. Therefore, when prices opened, the prices for each month were 3 to 4 fen to 7 to 8 fen lower than the previous day. However, because the national wheat falling order made stocks in the market tight, trading was not very busy. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading was still slow. However, because the flour market did not fall much and there were few sellers, prices rose again, recovering 4 to 5 fen compared to the morning. In the spot wheat market, high-grade goods had not opened, and second-grade goods prices remained stable. Shandong wheat opened at 6.05 yuan, Yanghe wheat at 6.05 yuan, Jue Ling wheat at 6.01 yuan, Yaowan wheat at 6.02 yuan, Bengbu wheat at 6.03 yuan, Hankou wheat at 5.8 yuan, Jiangbei wheat at 5.94 yuan, Huaian wheat at 5.97 yuan, and Chongming wheat at 5.75 yuan. Special Article The Food Problem in Times of Crisis

By Wo Sheng

Originally, the provinces and counties were already actively building warehouses, but for the sake of management, the warehouses in peacetime should be concentrated in each county, while in times of crisis, they should be distributed in various villages, and one should never put all eggs in one basket. The current Baojia system has been successful, and the existing local shrines and temples can be used as warehouses, which only requires a few carpentry and masonry jobs to establish community granaries. The chief of the Jia should be responsible for roughly calculating the amount of food needed by the local residents. Assuming one hundred households, averaging five people, then according to ancient precepts, one person needs two he of rice and one qian of salt, which means that each household needs one and a half dou of rice and ten jin of salt per day. Calculating the reserves for half a year, only six hundred shi of rice and twenty dan of salt are needed to avoid panic. If there is a shortfall, it should be purchased from outside as soon as possible, with a total value of no more than 2,000 yuan. If the chief of the Jia organizes a 500-yuan cooperative, with each share costing 5 yuan, plus a guarantee liability of four times, then they can borrow money from the bank to purchase goods. For every dan of grain stored in the community granary, 70% of the price should be paid first, and the remaining 30% should be paid in six installments. Then, a few long-term workers should be hired to hull and mill the rice, and the chief of the Jia should be responsible for this. A person should be sent by the bank to take custody of the granary, and the responsibility is only 1,000 yuan, so the person is easy to choose, and there is no need to worry about too many people. The actual situation of the community granary is easy to see, and there is a reliable guarantee on credit, and a People's Corps should be stationed in it to maintain order, and the danger of eating large households can also be avoided. On the bank's side, instead of bundling up banknotes and sending them out of the country, it is better to hide wealth among the people and make it circulate among the villages and towns to increase credit. When buying, banknotes are paid, and when selling, banknotes are also received. All chiefs of the Jia are elected by the heads of households, and they must have considerable credit and property. Therefore, I believe that the community granary system is very easy to implement, and it is also easy to prevent mildew and moths. Compared with centralized storage, it may produce many abuses, and it is difficult to relocate people and transport grain in times of crisis, which is not only half the effort but twice the result. As for paying 70% of the price, some may suspect that farmers will be reluctant. In fact, farmers always keep their own food after harvesting, and the reason why they are so eager to sell money is only 70% of the total. Today, in order to change money urgently, they are always killed in price and reluctantly give up, which is out of helplessness. Now, storing it in the society is more secure than storing it at home, regardless of whether it is for their own food. Under the Baojia system, it is not difficult to have sufficient food and troops to gain the trust of the people. I sincerely hope that our wise government will start doing it quickly. Jiaozi said, "The heavens have their own laws, which do not exist for Yao and do not perish for Jie." Therefore, I believe that regardless of whether it is a time of crisis or a time of peace, our people take food as their heaven, and we should act according to the laws of nature and fulfill our duties so that we will not be like the people of Qi who worry about the sky. However, in times of great chaos, the rural population will inevitably increase, so the amount of food reserves should be at least 30% more than usual.

Other

From the Women's Rights Movement to the Issue of Women's Self-Improvement

By Shou Zhuo

The call for women's rights movement does not seem to be a recent discovery; however, what achievements have the women's rights movement actually made? Perhaps no one can answer with certainty! The purpose of the women's rights movement, to put it bluntly, is to seek equality between men and women. It can also be said that women want to break away from their previous inhuman status and rise to the status of humans, enjoying the rights that humans should enjoy and fulfilling the obligations that humans should fulfill. Of course, this goal should be universally achieved, not partially achieved, otherwise partial solutions and temporary solutions are not fundamental solutions.

Although in today's China, women can be seen in agencies and shops, and women's works are sometimes seen in literary publications, it seems that the women's rights movement has had a considerable effect. However, if we ask how society evaluates female employees? And how many employed women are there? What kind of work do professional women do? We will suddenly realize and make a definite judgment: the women's movement is still waiting for our self-improvement efforts.

The current era is an era of survival of the fittest. Only the fittest can survive—to obtain the right to survive—only the best can win—to break the bad environment. We demand to be fit, we demand to be excellent, only through self-improvement and hard work, only through practical work. Shouting a few slogans and begging for sympathy is just a self-deceptive means. As for the necessary conditions for self-improvement and hard work, at least the following three points should be possessed.

(1) Having correct thoughts—Before any preparation, we must correct wrong ideas and establish correct thoughts, and we must know that our demands are to establish equality at the foundation, and it is by no means a single pursuit of rights or satisfaction of pleasure. For example, we are indeed demanding women's suffrage; however, we absolutely should not mistakenly think that women's work in operating and raising children at home is despicable. We only demand to have an equal spirit, and there should be no habit of favoring men over women in politics, education, and society. Whether we are officials, teachers, or doing family work, we all have the same importance. As for some young women who think that the purpose of the women's rights movement is to free women from the shackles of the family and enjoy freedom outside the family as much as possible, so they are unwilling to work for the family and cannot serve the society, and they only learn some fashionable language, and share benefits and enjoy pleasure in the society, as a result, they only increase the society's degree of contempt for women, all of which are the result of wrong thoughts.

(2) Having a strong physique—We know that doing everything requires a healthy physique. Women must assume half of the responsibilities of society and the country, so of course they must first have a healthy physique. However, Chinese women have always been famous for being sentimental and sickly. The lack of physical fitness is indeed undeniable. Therefore, the general public opinion in society always says that women's work efficiency is far inferior to that of men. Is that really the case for women? We do not see women in Soviet Russia participating in military work and bearing the same responsibilities as men. There are also many women in rural China who operate in the fields in the same way as men. Is this not a powerful refutation? Therefore, as long as we actively train, it is not difficult to have a healthy physique to assume major responsibilities. Now we urgently need to awaken public attention and use our best efforts to forge a strong physique.

(3) Having specialized skills—Having—Having correct thoughts and a healthy physique, we must also have specialized skills before we can take on important responsibilities and go far. The so-called specialized skills are by no means knowing some smattering, but having in-depth research and long-term training on a certain business or a certain job. Once we take on this task, we can not only cope with it easily, but also maximize our personal talents and seek good results. Regarding this point, we ask people who run women's education to pay attention to professional training, and at the same time, we hope that women who are currently studying will decide on a direction and concentrate on the cultivation of specialized skills. Of course, professional training must adapt to the needs of the environment and cater to individual ambitions and abilities. It is by no means asking everyone to cut their feet to fit their shoes and take the same path.

American Working Women

— by Lu Shaba

— A Dialogue on the Current State of Women's Occupations in Various Countries —

A: Lately, I often hear people say that women seeking liberation must first achieve equality in employment. This demand is naturally based on the principle of economic independence, but perhaps it also stems from seeing the development of women's occupations in advanced countries, leading to this "slogan." I would like to know about the situation of working women in various countries. Could you start by telling me about the current situation of American working women?

B: Sure, sure, we can sit down and talk. Please feel free to ask.

A: I would like to know about the social status of American working women.

B: Their social status is among the highest in the world. However, their self-awareness is not as strong as that of British working women, but their social status is much higher than that of other countries.

A: How much salary do they earn per day?

B: Their employment scope is very broad... From editors-in-chief of newspapers and company presidents to typists and female sales clerks in department stores, they all live a very comfortable life. However, it cannot be generalized. Of course, women who have their own capital to run businesses are excluded. On average, most people earn an annual income of $5,000. The lowest-paid American working women are female sales clerks in department stores and office workers without special skills. During the current economic downturn, wages have fallen accordingly, with a maximum of twelve US dollars a week (equivalent to 36 yuan in national currency). The wages of female servants are even lower. During prosperous times, black people could earn $700 a month, but since the economic panic, things are no longer the same. As long as they have a place to live and food to eat, they are willing to work for others, regardless of how much they get paid! However, black cooks with skills still have very high salaries... Good white female servants can earn $35 a month. Many general working women work as stenographers and typists, earning $25 to $28 a week. Female secretaries can earn $60 to $100 a month.

A: Now I remember, let me ask about the departments where women work?

B: The number of women employed is not much different from that of men. They participate in every occupational department and occupy a fairly important position. In politics, they also hold important positions such as county magistrates, mayors, and ambassadors. They also participate in various investigation and research work, such as scientific research institutes and mechanical engineering architectural design. This is rare for Chinese women. Because these women are engaged in high-level technical work that uses their brains, they receive more compensation.

A: Is the social infrastructure for working women in the United States complete?

B: The social infrastructure in the United States is quite developed.

A: Are there facilities such as daycare centers in the United States?

B: There are no facilities specifically established for working women, but their nature is the same as that of daycare centers.

A: When working women are sick, does the state have sanatoriums or other facilities?

B: Although the state does not have such facilities, each district also has public hospitals under the name of social undertakings, and medical expenses are only charged half price.

A: Are they concerned about politics? At what age do they have the right to vote? Do they abstain from voting during elections?

B: They are relatively concerned about politics. Generally, women have the right to vote at the age of twenty-one. Female workers in factories are mostly organized, so their political awareness is more obvious, and abstentions are rare. Some ordinary women pay more attention to politics, but most of them take a don't-ask-don't-tell attitude, and some even give up their right to vote.

The Duty of Female Clerks

— by Cheng Peizhen

When women in our community serve in society, in addition to having considerable knowledge and experience, they must also have a spirit of thrift, a humble attitude, and honest character. Then, the future development of our female clerks in various fields will be unlimited. If, once they have a position, they hold a proud attitude, extravagant desires, and romantic disposition, applying rouge and powder, and having disheveled hair, only engaging in dressing up, without taking their own duties as a prerequisite, then not only will they not fit the identity of a female clerk, but they will also have the nickname of a "vase," which is really a move to lower their own personality! Female clerks who like to show off are greatly tabooed by any organization or store, which is very unfavorable to their own future. Moreover, the monthly salary is limited. Why must the hard-earned money be spent on extravagant decorations!

It must be known that the intention of public institutions and capitalists to hire female clerks is to promote the development of women's careers and to seek a livelihood for women. Because women's work spirit is relatively meticulous, their temperament is also more gentle, and their salaries are slightly lower than those of male clerks. On the one hand, they cater to the psychology of the public, which can attract customers, "customers are happy with the amiable female clerks," which is of great importance to the future of the business. They are not hiring a few female clerks to serve as vase-like decorations! I hope that our dear female comrades will unite together, maintain their inherent personality and credit, and promote the development of our women's rights. Our 200 million female compatriots across the country will also have glory.

As for the public institutions, there are also many female comrades working here. Their knowledge and experience are relatively more noble. Of course, they are much less interested in unnecessary luxury and vanity! However, female clerks with higher positions are inevitably infected by material civilization in social occasions, which is a major reason for the unstable lives of some women in society. Especially women who live in big cities, those who can be thrifty and keep themselves clean are indeed rare and valuable people.

In short, since we women have considerable occupations, we can be economically independent, and can reduce part of the burden of fathers, brothers, or husbands, and can also supplement the insufficiency of family finances. In general, women cannot fail to understand the heavy burden of fathers, brothers, or husbands, and the difficulty of making a living.

Taking advantage of writing this article, I will write down the thrift and hardworking spirit of my friend, Ms. Sun Yingxue.

She is a 24-year-old girl from a poor family who lost her education in her childhood and only has an elementary school education. Five years ago, she entered the export department of a foreign firm as a small female clerk with a monthly salary of only twelve yuan. Because she is diligent in her work and has a humble nature, the manager of the firm also values her very much. Her knowledge and experience have also gradually improved. Now she has been promoted to the management director of the export department female clerks, and there are twelve female clerks under her command, so her future is also unlimited.

Her salary has gradually increased to thirty-five yuan. As for her daily life, she only rents a small room, with a rent of four yuan. The monthly expenditure is less than fifteen yuan. Her clothing is simple, and the decoration is simple, which is beyond the reach of ordinary people. She only needs to eat a few hundred cents of food every day. At noon, she only buys a bowl of plain noodles to fill her hunger in the firm. Her thriftiness is indeed not forgetting the poverty of losing her parents early in her childhood. Therefore, she has not been to amusement parks or movie theaters for a year. On Saturday afternoons and Sundays, she does some laundry and needlework and knits woolen threads, so her financial situation is also very affluent. She now has savings of one thousand and several hundred yuan. In short, her savings come from thrift and hard work. Ms. Sun's character and work spirit are a good example worthy of worship in our women's community!

Wash away the dirt and return my purity

Rural Women During Rice Harvesting Season

— by Delin

Now it is the rice harvesting season. The autumn countryside is a scene of wealth and responsibility. The fields are full of laughter from farmers, both men and women. The picture of a joyous year with chickens and wine will be unfolded in the corners of bamboo fences, thatched huts, and rubble walls. Autumn! Lovely autumn, actually covering the usually barren fields with gold, waiting for people to collect it.

At this time, the farmers are working hard to thresh the rice. If you go to the countryside, you will see them waving in the autumn sun; those cut down and lying crisscrossed in the fields are not the fruitful and golden ears of rice? This is the price of hard work and sweat; this is the reward for hard work and dedication. Look, those who are crawling in the fields to cut rice; those who are carrying it on the paths, are not those hard-working farmers, both men and women?

Golden and fluffy hair, the bun dragged to the back! "The oily sweat flows on the forehead like winding little rivers. The two breasts rising in front tremble with each step. The small legs covered with mud, like a muddy lotus root, walk on the plain, put the burden in the corner of the chicken coop and cattle shed, run into the mud-brick thatched hut, untie the buttons of the clothes, bend the waist and put the nipples into the mouth of the infant who is not yet one year old and sleeping in the bamboo bed, shake the bamboo bed, and hum the tune of "rocking, baby, sleep for a while" in the mouth. What a simple life these rural women live, working hard all day long. In addition to working in the fields during the day, they also have to wash clothes, cook, and feed the baby. The ladies, young ladies, and young mistresses in the city are dedicated to fighting each other and competing for beauty, enjoying a superior life. Have they ever spent their hard work and sweat? They only use their bodies to seduce and exchange, and eventually become parasites of men, without even realizing it.

Special report from this newspaper

Ms. Xie Zuyi Talks About the Young Women's Movement

— by Ping

Young women must know their own responsibilities and have an independent personality! Automatically seek improvement in life and upward consciousness!

Since moving to Jing'an Temple Road, the Shanghai Young Women's Christian Association (YWCA) has a much more spacious building than the one on Yuanmingyuan Road, and its activities have also developed considerably. However, this YWCA is still far behind the YMCA. Is it really that women are no match for men? I hope that the women's community will also rise up together, unite and work hard to fully demonstrate the spirit of women serving society. Some people say that in the past year, under the planning and management of General Secretary Xie Zuyi, the association has made much more progress than before. Speaking of Ms. Xie's knowledge and talent, it is indeed very superior. She is originally from Sichuan. She grew up in Shanghai Chinese and Western Girls' School. After graduation, she stayed in the United States for six years and obtained a Master of Arts in Sociology from the University of Chicago. When she was studying in the United States, she had done practical work in the YWCA. She felt that studying sociology should be related to the real society and engaging in the movement to improve society. So doing this work is exactly what she learned. It was also a coincidence. Last year, when she returned to Shanghai, she was honored to be the General Secretary. The other day, I went to visit her and asked her to express her opinions on the young women's movement. There are two main points that can be reported to readers.

(1)

Until now, many people still do not understand the purpose of the young women's movement. The YWCA is actually a group of women who are transforming society. It is a social education mechanism and a pioneer of the women's movement; leading countless enthusiastic young women, based on Christ's mission to transform society, cultivating women's self-awareness and solidarity. It is international and permanent. No matter what country it is, monarchical and democratic, or dictatorial and communist, there are YWCA organizations. For example, in the Soviet Union, there is no YWCA in name, but similar women's groups still exist. The so-called self-awareness means that every woman must understand her own responsibility to the society and the country, and the independent and upward personality, without being reminded by others, she must first realize it herself. The so-called solidarity means that each self-aware woman should unite together to seek her own liberation or participate in any movement, so that there is strength. Only then can the ultimate goal be achieved. The YWCA organizes women from all walks of life, so that they can automatically seek improvement in life and upward consciousness. The members include working women, working women, housewives, and general young women. According to the different ages and interests of all aspects, various effective trainings are implemented, and everyone's experience is exchanged, so that everyone feels satisfied. For example, for upper-class women and the intellectual class, the YWCA wants to awaken them to recognize the meaning of life, and use their talents, knowledge and money to assist others, and create leaders who serve all mankind. For lower-class women, enable them to increase their ability, seek their own liberation, and not rely on others to be pitiful parasites!

(2)

Our wish is that the YWCA will become a true central group for women from all walks of life. All work should not only have a close relationship with the women's community and seek the common happiness of the women's community; it must also have a relationship with all aspects of society, so that the outside world knows that this is a large group of women who are raising women's rights and doing practical work. Since the association moved into the new system last year, it has been very convenient to promote the association's affairs, and the necessary equipment is complete. The association is divided into eight departments: adult education, mass education, labor, young women, career introduction, dormitory, sports, and international branch. In terms of work: according to the needs of women from all walks of life, research societies (child psychology, current affairs research, women's issues, healthy living, etc.), friendship societies, visiting groups, celebrity speeches, travel, summer camps, and tutoring classes (foreign languages, home economics, social interaction, music, typing, etc.) are established. The association undertakes various affairs with the support of social women and men, seeking the highest efficiency of service with the most economical methods. We hope that all female compatriots in Shanghai can support us and participate in our activities to seek the well-being and harmony of the masses!

(3)

Ms. Xie also expressed some feelings about women's careers: 1. Now, young people in general show negative and disappointed emotions when they first come out to work, half because they are not diligent and half because they are limited by the environment and cannot develop their talents; and most women have too few opportunities to serve. In the future, I hope that men will give women more opportunities to serve. Women themselves should fully train and prepare themselves during their school years so that they can cope with all arduous tasks. At present, there is no talent in the women's community. In some places, the work of "discovering talent" cannot be done. Some people often criticize women for not being effective in their work. In fact, they use private individuals, private individuals with mediocre talents. Therefore, I say that from government agencies to companies and shops, it is necessary to select true talents and not bury brave and promising young people. Opportunities for employment in the vocational community must be completely equal and the vast avenues must be opened up as much as possible, so that everyone can use their talents to the best of their ability. Women must be self-aware and strive hard. The value of women will naturally increase and there will be a way out for liberation!

Ms. Xie Zuyi

The Subconscious (Part Two)

— by Yin

The seats on the highway bus were not comfortable at all. Five people in a row were almost full, and it was difficult to turn around. When Yifan got on the bus, there were only three seats left on the last row, but that fat man was quick to grab one, and he squeezed Yifan away. He grabbed a seat by the window for himself, arranged his wife in the second one, and the innermost one—the most uncomfortable one in the center—was a favor he did to Yifan. And because he was too fat, he and his wife occupied two and a quarter seats in total. The seat Yifan occupied was not even one full seat, so he had to squeeze in reluctantly.

The fat military officer was naturally unnoticed, but his wife became the focus of all fourteen men in the car (there were only three women). Since Yifan got on the bus with them in front of the hostel and sat down next to her, he had never paid attention to her. Now he saw everyone staring at her in a daze, so he felt that he also had to take a look at her.

Of course, he looked at her. What was his impression after taking a look? Yifan's preconceived notion that the Northwest was a desert could not stand after this look. At the same time, he felt that a beautiful woman like her should not be traveling with that fat and stupid military officer. If that military officer had really abused her last night, it was an unforgivable and heinous crime. Because of this feeling, he was filled with pity and hatred. The pity was for the woman, and the hatred was for the military officer.

The military officer lowered his head and snored soon after getting on the bus. Moreover, he leaned his fat body against his wife as if his life depended on it. His wife looked very haggard, but she did not want to sleep, as if she was worried about something. However, she could not support her husband's fat body, so she leaned over to Yifan's side. Yifan saw that there was an old woman with white hair on his left, so of course he could not lean over to her. He had to use some strength to support them reluctantly. At this time, half of the woman's body was almost leaning on Yifan; her fluffy hair and mysterious fragrance immediately made Yifan, who had never been close to the opposite sex, feel a mysterious stimulus. He almost decided to use force to squeeze them back, but he felt that he could not bear to do so, because he knew that doing so would definitely make the military officer's wife in the middle attacked from both sides. He had to endure it reluctantly. However, another layer of difficulty arose, that is, his own line of sight, somehow, insisted on concentrating on the face of this military officer's wife and all other parts of her body, and the eyes of this military officer's wife seemed to be paying attention to him, and revealing a kind of amorous expression. Yifan felt that this was too dangerous, but luckily he had a few novels with him, so he took one out to look at. Unexpectedly, the woman also felt too bored, so she leaned closer and looked at it with him. It was very difficult for Yifan to see it from afar, so he simply handed the novel over and took one out himself. She did not refuse, but smiled sweetly at him. This smile distracted Yifan's attention from reading. Although his eyes were on her, he could not see the words on the book. It was as if they had all turned into white paper. Sometimes he would also slant his eyeballs and steal a glance at her. She did not seem to notice that Yifan was looking at her, but the page numbers on her book had not turned for a long time, and she read about ten minutes for one page. Later, she took out a lipstick from her wallet and wrote on Yifan's book: "Last name?" Yifan only whispered the word Liu; she wrote "Going? To," and Yifan, only Lanzhou. She wrote another "Together." Yifan gradually became bolder, so he pouted his mouth to the military officer and quietly asked, "Who is he?" She was still not answering, and wrote the word "Evil." As soon as this word was written, the two of them could not help but sigh at the same time. Fortunately, no one else noticed, so they secretly talked to each other with one question and one answer, and by the time the car arrived at a certain place, they were already very familiar with each other. Yifan's right hand and her left hand had also been tightly held together for two or three hours; later, she also wrote "Escape," "Escape" in large letters on the book. Yifan really did not have this courage, so he had to quietly comfort her and said, "Let's discuss it again when we get to Lanzhou."

That night, everyone was roughing it out near the station. Yifan really could not get used to that dirty pit life. He had not fallen asleep by midnight. He was sitting under a dim kerosene lamp, thinking blankly about the lovers he had met on the bus. Suddenly, he heard someone knocking on the door, followed by a trembling woman's voice arguing with the landlord. Yifan hurriedly rushed out to see what was going on. It was really her. As soon as she saw him, she rushed over and hugged him into the house. Before Yifan could sit down, she rushed to tell him that her husband had just received an emergency order and had left on a military vehicle. Yifan did not know whether to be happy or sad, but he felt that his heart was about to jump out of his chest.

The next day, the two of them changed to a Xi'an car in a very flustered manner and eloped. At that time, Yifan had completely forgotten about his first sculpture that was about to be published. However, he did not dare to go back to Shanghai, because he was afraid that his father would scold him; however, from then on, he really could not go back, because the news of his elopement with the military officer's wife soon spread in newspapers everywhere, and the sculptor Liu Yifan became a sinner spurned by society. Everyone was ridiculing:

"The subconscious! The subconscious!"

Today, we are delighted to celebrate the 50th birthday of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. This journal respectfully represents all female compatriots across the country to wish him a long life! And may Chairman Chiang Kai-shek lead the entire nation with the spirit of fearlessness and save the dying China! Zhou Shoujuan, Huang Jiping, Respectful greetings

Shenbao Local Supplement

Miraculous Pivot and Plain Questions

— Doctor Liu Xinbai, Chief Respondent

Knowledge for Those Seeking Medical Advice (Issue 9)

1. Letters should be sent to our clinic: 1108 Qinyuan Village, Xinwen Road, Shanghai (East of Gordon Road).

2. Letters must be written in vernacular Chinese.

3. Do not use vague terms like "wind," "fire," or "heat," which are abstract and lack specific meaning when describing illnesses.

4. Describe your symptoms as detailed as possible.

5. Please enclose postage stamps with your letters: five cents for out-of-town mail, two cents for local mail. If I deem the case lacking public value, I will reply directly by mail.

6. Please clearly write the patient's detailed address.

7. Medical consultations by mail are free. In-person consultations are limited to 3:00 PM to 5:00 PM, charged at half the rate of a regular consultation. Sundays are limited to mornings.

8. When asking about several aspects of one illness in a single letter—such as the origin, symptoms, disease, severity, and treatment—please number each question.

9. Medical inquiries are limited to internal medicine and dermatology/venereology. Questions outside this scope will not be answered.

10. This column will publicly answer questions once every Saturday.

Scrofula

No. 64, Mr. Peng Shuchen from Tongan Lane, Xinma Road, Nanshi asks: A friend's wife is reportedly not virtuous. According to her husband, "A lump has grown where her left leg connects to her lower abdomen, and it is growing larger every day. He immediately asked a Chinese medicine doctor to inject '606,' but the swelling worsened after the injection. The center of the lump has softened." He asks: (1) Is this syphilis? (2) Was there a mistake in the 606 injection? (3) What is a reliable treatment? (4) Does this illness constitute grounds for divorce?

Answer: (1) It is not syphilis, it is scrofula. (2) It was already incorrect for the Chinese medicine doctor to inject 606; injecting an anti-syphilis drug into scrofula is completely absurd. (3) The center has softened, indicating it has festered. Please see a doctor to have it incised. Before it festered, injecting Teku-pin and using Mecuary ointment might have reduced it, but that is no longer possible. (4) This is a legal question, so I will not answer it.

Pubic Lice

No. 65, Mr. Sun Xiaobao from Laobaisheng Branch Road, Caojiadu asks: My husband does not behave properly and frequents prostitutes, despite my earnest advice. Two days after intimacy with my husband, my vulva became unbearably itchy, and there are eight-legged lice on my pubic hair, which are impossible to catch all of. There is also something that looks like yellow sand on my pubic hair. Therefore, I ask: (1) What is this illness? (2) Is it related to venereal disease? (3) How can it be cured? (4) What is the yellow sand?

Answer: (1) Pubic lice. (2) It comes from unclean sexual intercourse, but it is unrelated to venereal disease. (3) Apply 2% Neochrome. (4) Lice eggs.

Eliminating Roundworms

No. 66, Mr. Duan Jingbi from Zhangjiazhai, Aiwenyi Road asks: My eldest son is five years old this year. Although he eats a lot, he does not gain weight, his complexion is yellow, he is weak, his belly is large, and he often scratches his anus. Sometimes he excretes roundworms that look like fly larvae. The doctor said they were roundworms, so I bought goosefoot and fed it to him. Although he excreted many, he is not completely cured. He asks: (1) Are these roundworms? (2) What medicine is most reliable? (3) Are you confident in treating this disease?

Answer: (1) They are pinworms, not roundworms. (2) Inject Santoninsol and use a 5% Tryierin solution for enemas every day. (3) Yes.

Intending to Quit Opium

No. 67, Mr. Zhang Zhongfu from Yugu Village, Yuwei Road asks: I previously discussed with my friend Mr. Song your methods of quitting opium, and I admire them greatly. I have been trapped by opium for a long time and cannot stop freely. Moreover, the National Government has issued clear orders, so I also intend to ask you to help me escape this bitter sea. However, I have several questions to ask, please reply in detail: (1) I have been using opium for ten years, will there be any problems quitting? (2) I have a history of back pain, will it recur during the quitting period? (3) Is it necessary to inject, and if so, what medicine?

Answer: (1) No problem. (2) Possible. (3) It varies depending on individual constitution, but injecting Antiopin during the quitting period and injecting phosmin after quitting are indispensable.

No. 68, Answer to Mr. Zhang Anyi from Xiangrui Lane, Haining Road: (1) Gonorrhea and syphilis can be transmitted simultaneously. (2) The small particles are not syphilis or gonorrhea, but red tinea. (3) Blood tests at the health bureau are reliable.

(2) Treatment is described in (1). It cannot be treated by applying medicine yourself. (3) There is no need to circumcise. (4) It is a type of venereal disease.

Announcement: In the future, please do not ask in letters how much medicines or injections cost, as it has no value and is not worth a reply.

Chancre

Cessation of Menstruation

They prescribed strong and hot remedies such as "donkey-hide gelatin," "dried ginger," and "fish roe," but they were ineffective. (According to her, the patient dislikes heat and usually takes cooling remedies.)
